_**Back to the Future**_ is a 1985 American [science fiction film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_fiction_film "Science fiction film") directed by [Robert Zemeckis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Zemeckis "Robert Zemeckis") and written by Zemeckis and [Bob Gale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Gale "Bob Gale"). It stars [Michael J. Fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_J._Fox "Michael J. Fox"), [Christopher Lloyd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Lloyd "Christopher Lloyd"), [Lea Thompson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lea_Thompson "Lea Thompson"), [Crispin Glover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crispin_Glover "Crispin Glover"), and [Thomas F. Wilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_F._Wilson "Thomas F. Wilson"). Set in 1985, it follows [Marty McFly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marty_McFly "Marty McFly") (Fox), a teenager accidentally sent back to 1955 in a [time-traveling DeLorean automobile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DeLorean_time_machine "DeLorean time machine") built by his eccentric scientist friend [Emmett "Doc" Brown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmett_Brown "Emmett Brown") (Lloyd), where he inadvertently prevents his future parents from falling in love – threatening his own existence – and is forced to reconcile them and somehow get back to the future.

Gale and Zemeckis conceived the idea for _Back to the Future_ in 1980. They were desperate for a successful film after numerous collaborative failures, but the project was rejected more than forty times by various studios because it was not considered raunchy enough to compete with the successful comedies of the era. A development deal was secured with [Universal Pictures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Pictures "Universal Pictures") following Zemeckis's success directing _[Romancing the Stone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romancing_the_Stone "Romancing the Stone")_ (1984). Fox was the first choice to portray Marty but was unavailable; [Eric Stoltz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Stoltz "Eric Stoltz") was cast instead. Shortly after [principal photography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principal_photography "Principal photography") began in November 1984, Zemeckis determined Stoltz was not right for the part and made the concessions necessary to hire Fox, including re-filming scenes already shot with Stoltz and adding $4million to the budget. _Back to the Future_ was filmed in and around California and on sets at [Universal Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Studios_Lot "Universal Studios Lot"), and concluded the following April.

After highly successful test screenings, the release date was brought forward to July3, 1985, giving the film more time in theaters during the busiest period of the theatrical year. The change resulted in a rushed post-production schedule and some incomplete special effects. Nevertheless, _Back to the Future_ was a critical and commercial success, earning $381.1million to become the [highest-grossing film of 1985](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985_in_film "1985 in film") worldwide. Critics praised the story, humor, and the cast, particularly Fox, Lloyd, Thompson, and Glover. It received multiple award nominations and won an [Academy Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/58th_Academy_Awards "58th Academy Awards"), three [Saturn Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/13th_Saturn_Awards "13th Saturn Awards"), and a [Hugo Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugo_Award_for_Best_Dramatic_Presentation "Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation"). Its theme song, " [The Power of Love](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Power_of_Love_(Huey_Lewis_and_the_News_song) "The Power of Love (Huey Lewis and the News song)")" by [Huey Lewis and the News](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huey_Lewis_and_the_News "Huey Lewis and the News"), was also a success.

_Back to the Future_ has since grown in esteem and is now considered by critics and audiences to be one of the greatest science fiction films and among the [best films ever made](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_films_considered_the_best "List of films considered the best"). In 2007, the United States [Library of Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_of_Congress "Library of Congress") selected it for preservation in the [National Film Registry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Film_Registry "National Film Registry"). The film was followed by two sequels, _[Back to the Future Part II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_Part_II "Back to the Future Part II")_ (1989) and _[Back to the Future Part III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_Part_III "Back to the Future Part III")_ (1990). Spurred by the film's dedicated fan following and effect on popular culture, Universal Studios launched [a multimedia franchise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_(franchise) "Back to the Future (franchise)"), which now includes [video games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Back_to_the_Future_video_games "List of Back to the Future video games"), [theme park rides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future:_The_Ride "Back to the Future: The Ride"), [an animated television series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_(TV_series) "Back to the Future (TV series)"), and [a stage musical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future:_The_Musical "Back to the Future: The Musical"). Its enduring popularity has prompted numerous books about its production, documentaries, and commercials.

## Plot

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Plot")\]

In 1985, teenager [Marty McFly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marty_McFly "Marty McFly") lives in [Hill Valley, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hill_Valley_(Back_to_the_Future) "Hill Valley (Back to the Future)"), with his depressed alcoholic mother, [Lorraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorraine_Baines-McFly "Lorraine Baines-McFly"); his older siblings, who are professional and social failures; and his meek father, [George](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_McFly "George McFly"), who is bullied by his supervisor, [Biff Tannen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biff_Tannen "Biff Tannen"). After Marty's band fails a music audition, he confides in his girlfriend, Jennifer Parker, that he fears becoming like his parents despite his ambitions.

That night, Marty meets his eccentric scientist friend, [Emmett "Doc" Brown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmett_Brown "Emmett Brown"), in the [Twin Pines mall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twin_Pines_Mall "Twin Pines Mall") parking lot. Doc unveils a [time machine built from a modified DeLorean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DeLorean_time_machine "DeLorean time machine"), powered by [plutonium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plutonium "Plutonium") he swindled from Libyan terrorists. After Doc inputs a destination time of November 5, 1955 (the day he first conceived his time travel invention), the terrorists arrive unexpectedly and gun him down. Marty flees in the DeLorean, inadvertently activating time travel when he reaches 88 miles per hour (142 kilometers per hour).

Arriving in 1955, Marty discovers he has no plutonium, so he cannot return to 1985. While exploring a burgeoning Hill Valley, Marty encounters his teenage father and discovers Biff was bullying George even then. George falls into the path of an oncoming car while [spying](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voyeurism "Voyeurism") on the teenage Lorraine changing clothes, and Marty is knocked unconscious while saving him. He wakes to find himself tended to by Lorraine, who becomes infatuated with him. Marty tracks down and convinces a younger Doc that he is from the future, but Doc explains the only source available in 1955 capable of generating the 1.21 gigawatts of power required for time travel is a lightning bolt. Marty shows Doc a flyer from the future that documents an upcoming lightning strike at the town's courthouse. As Marty's siblings begin to fade from a photo he carries with him, Doc realizes Marty's actions are [altering the future](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temporal_paradox#Grandfather_paradox "Temporal paradox") and jeopardizing his existence: Lorraine was supposed to tend to George instead of Marty after the car accident. Early attempts to get his parents acquainted fail, and Lorraine's infatuation with Marty deepens.

Lorraine asks Marty to the school dance, and he plots to feign inappropriate advances on her, allowing George to intervene and rescue her, but the plan goes awry when Biff's gang locks Marty in the trunk of the performing band's car, while Biff forces himself onto Lorraine. George arrives expecting to find Marty but is assaulted by Biff. After Biff hurts Lorraine, an enraged George knocks him unconscious and escorts the grateful Lorraine to the dance. The band frees Marty from their car, but the lead guitarist injures his hand in the process, so Marty takes his place, performing while George and Lorraine share their first kiss. With his future no longer in jeopardy, Marty hurries to the courthouse to meet Doc.

Doc discovers a letter from Marty warning him about his future and rips it up, worried about the consequences. To save Doc, Marty recalibrates the DeLorean to return ten minutes before he had left the future. The lightning strikes, sending Marty back to 1985, but the DeLorean breaks down, forcing Marty to run back to the mall. He arrives as Doc is being shot. While Marty grieves at his side, Doc sits up, revealing he had pieced Marty's note back together and is wearing a bulletproof vest. He takes Marty home and departs to 2015 in the DeLorean. Marty wakes the next morning to discover his father is now a confident and successful [science fiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_fiction "Science fiction") author, his mother is fit and happy, his siblings are successful, and Biff is a servile valet in George's employ. As Marty reunites with Jennifer, Doc suddenly reappears in the DeLorean, insisting they return with him to the future to save their children from terrible fates.[\[a\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-2)

## Cast

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: Cast")\]

See also: [List of _Back to the Future_ characters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Back_to_the_Future_characters "List of Back to the Future characters")

[![A photograph of Michael J Fox](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Michael_J._Fox_1985_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Michael_J._Fox_1985_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Michael_J._Fox_1985_(cropped).jpg)

[![A photograph of Christopher Lloyd](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/ChristopherLloydOct10.jpg/250px-ChristopherLloydOct10.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ChristopherLloydOct10.jpg)

[Michael J. Fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_J._Fox "Michael J. Fox") in 1985 (left) and [Christopher Lloyd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Lloyd "Christopher Lloyd") in 2010

- [Michael J. Fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_J._Fox "Michael J. Fox") as Marty McFly, a high school student and aspiring musician[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LevyRevisit-3)
- [Christopher Lloyd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Lloyd "Christopher Lloyd") as Emmett "Doc" Brown, an eccentric scientist experimenting with time travel[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ASCILM-4)
- [Lea Thompson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lea_Thompson "Lea Thompson") as Lorraine Baines McFly, a 1955 teenager who grows into Marty's unhappy, alcoholic mother[\[4\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevVariety-5)
- [Crispin Glover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crispin_Glover "Crispin Glover") as George McFly, a nerdy 1955 high schooler who grows into Marty's cowardly, submissive father[\[4\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevVariety-5)
- [Thomas F. Wilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_F._Wilson "Thomas F. Wilson") as Biff Tannen, a 1955 high school bully turned George's 1985 boss[\[5\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LooperBiff-6)

The 1985 portion of the film features a cast including [Claudia Wells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claudia_Wells "Claudia Wells") as Marty's girlfriend Jennifer Parker, and [Marc McClure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marc_McClure "Marc McClure") and [Wendie Jo Sperber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wendie_Jo_Sperber "Wendie Jo Sperber") as Marty's siblings [Dave McFly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Back_to_the_Future_characters#Dave_McFly "List of Back to the Future characters") and [Linda McFly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linda_McFly "Linda McFly").[\[6\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985July3Maslin-7) [Elsa Raven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elsa_Raven "Elsa Raven") plays the Clocktower Lady. Singer [Huey Lewis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huey_Lewis "Huey Lewis") has a cameo role as a judge for the Battle of the Bands contest.[\[7\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-USATodayLewis-8)[\[8\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ShortlistDudley-9) RichardL. Duran and Jeff O'Haco portray the Libyan terrorists.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AFI-1)

Cast appearing in the 1955 portion includes [George DiCenzo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_DiCenzo "George DiCenzo") and [Frances Lee McCain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frances_Lee_McCain "Frances Lee McCain") as Lorraine's parents, Sam and Stella Baines,[\[6\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985July3Maslin-7) and [Jason Hervey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jason_Hervey "Jason Hervey") as Lorraine's younger brother Milton. Biff's gang includes [Jeffrey Jay Cohen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._J._Cohen "J. J. Cohen") as Skinhead, [Casey Siemaszko](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casey_Siemaszko "Casey Siemaszko") as 3-D, and [Billy Zane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billy_Zane "Billy Zane") as Match. [Norman Alden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norman_Alden "Norman Alden") plays cafe owner Lou, and [Donald Fullilove](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Fullilove "Donald Fullilove") appears as his employee (and future mayor) Goldie Wilson. [Harry Waters Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Waters_Jr. "Harry Waters Jr.") portrays [Chuck Berry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuck_Berry "Chuck Berry")'s cousin Marvin Berry; [Will Hare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Will_Hare "Will Hare") appears as PaPeabody; and [Courtney Gains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Courtney_Gains "Courtney Gains") portrays Dixon, the youth who interrupts George's and Lorraine's dance.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AFI-1) [James Tolkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Tolkan "James Tolkan") portrays Hill Valley high school principal [Strickland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Back_to_the_Future_characters#Gerald_Strickland "List of Back to the Future characters") in both 1955 and 1985.[\[6\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985July3Maslin-7)

## Production

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Production")\]

### Conception and writing

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: Conception and writing")\]

[![Robert Zemeckis](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Robert_Zemeckis_by_David_Shankbone.jpg/250px-Robert_Zemeckis_by_David_Shankbone.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Robert_Zemeckis_by_David_Shankbone.jpg) Director [Robert Zemeckis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Zemeckis "Robert Zemeckis") in 2010, who developed _Back to the Future_ with his long-time friend Bob Gale

Long-time collaborators [Bob Gale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Gale "Bob Gale") and [Robert Zemeckis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Zemeckis "Robert Zemeckis") conceived _Back to the Future_ in 1980.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11)[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HFPAOralHistory-12) They wanted to develop a film about time travel but struggled to create a satisfying narrative, and were desperate for a successful project after the critical or commercial failures of their recent efforts in collaboration with Zemeckis's mentor, [Steven Spielberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steven_Spielberg "Steven Spielberg").[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11)[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HFPAOralHistory-12)

Following the release of their comedy _[Used Cars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Used_Cars "Used Cars")_ (1980), Gale visited his parents and came across his father's high school [yearbook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yearbook "Yearbook").[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HFPAOralHistory-12)[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesGaleJul85-13) He wondered if he and his father would have been friends had they attended school together. He did not think so, but realized he could test his theory if he could travel back to a time when he and his parents were a similar age.[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesGaleJul85-13) He shared the idea with Zemeckis, who recalled his mother's childhood stories were often contradictory.[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HFPAOralHistory-12)

Gale and Zemeckis began a draft in late 1980. They sketched and acted out each scene to help develop the dialogue and actions.[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesGaleJul85-13) They believed many time-travel films focused on the past being immutable and wanted to show the past being altered and the effect those changes would have on the future.[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HFPAOralHistory-12) In the draft, [video pirate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copyright_infringement "Copyright infringement") Professor Brown builds a time machine that sends his young friend Marty back to the 1950s where he interrupts his parents' first meeting.[\[13\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201512-14) In September 1980, Gale and Zemeckis pitched their idea to [Columbia Pictures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbia_Pictures "Columbia Pictures") president [Frank Price](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Price "Frank Price"), who had liked _Used Cars_ and was keen to work with the pair. Gale recalled having to rein in Zemeckis's enthusiastic pitch before Price had time to change his mind.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) Gale and Zemeckis completed the first draft for Price on February21, 1981, but Price believed it needed significant refinement.[\[13\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201512-14)

Some early concepts were abandoned. Originally, Marty's actions in 1955 had a more significant impact on the future, making 1985 more futuristic and advanced, but every person who read the script took issue with the idea.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15) Marty's father also became a boxer, a result of his knockout punch on Biff.[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15) The time machine was a stationary object moved around on the back of a truck.[\[8\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ShortlistDudley-9)[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)[\[15\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SlashFilmFridge-16) Inspired by the documentary _[The Atomic Cafe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Atomic_Cafe "The Atomic Cafe")_, the drained time machine was written to be powered by Marty driving it into a nuclear explosion, combined with an additional ingredient: [Coca-Cola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coca-Cola "Coca-Cola").[\[b\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-19) Gale and Zemeckis took inspiration from tales of legendary scientists, opting to make the time machine's creator an individual instead of a faceless corporation or government.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10) The pair wanted the inciting time-travel incident to be an accident so that it would not appear that the hero was seeking personal gain.[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)

Gale and Zemeckis drew humor from the cultural contrasts between 1955 and 1985, such as Marty entering a 1955 soda shop in 1985 clothing; the shop owner asks Marty if he is a sailor because his down vest resembles a [life preserver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personal_flotation_device#Life_jacket "Personal flotation device"). They also identified conveniences of 1985 that Marty had taken for granted, but would be denied in 1955. Gale and Zemeckis struggled with the writing, as they were in their 30s and did not particularly identify with either era.[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesGaleJul85-13) They were inspired by the [All-American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All-American "All-American") aesthetic of films by [Frank Capra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Capra "Frank Capra") featuring [white picket fences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Picket_fence "Picket fence") and exaggerated characters similar to Biff,[\[18\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ShortList-20) _[The Twilight Zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Twilight_Zone_(1959_TV_series) "The Twilight Zone (1959 TV series)")_, science fiction films, and books by [Robert Silverberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Silverberg "Robert Silverberg") and [Robert Heinlein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Heinlein "Robert Heinlein").[\[19\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-CNNGaleInterview-21) The romantic relationship between 1955 Lorraine and her future son was one of the more difficult writing challenges.[\[20\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesJun1985AttheMovies-22) Gale and Zemeckis attempted to take the concept as far as possible to keep the audience on edge. They believed it had to be Lorraine who stopped the relationship; she remarks that kissing Marty feels like kissing her brother. Gale jokingly said no one asked how she could make that comparison, but that audiences would accept it because they did not want the relationship to happen.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) The second draft was completed by April7, 1981.[\[13\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201512-14)

### Development

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: Development")\]

[![Steven Spielberg shown talking into a microphone](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Steven_Spielberg_-_GianAngelo_Pistoia_1_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Steven_Spielberg_-_GianAngelo_Pistoia_1_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Steven_Spielberg_-_GianAngelo_Pistoia_1_(cropped).jpg) [Steven Spielberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steven_Spielberg "Steven Spielberg") in 1993. He mentored Zemeckis and lent his experience and Hollywood studio clout to support the production of _Back to the Future_.

Price opted not to [green-light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green-light "Green-light") the second draft; although he liked it, he did not believe it would appeal to anyone else.[\[21\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201512,_13-23) The most successful comedies at the time, such as _[Animal House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_House "Animal House")_ (1978), _[Porky's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Porky%27s "Porky's")_ (1981), and _[Fast Times at Ridgemont High](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fast_Times_at_Ridgemont_High "Fast Times at Ridgemont High")_ (1982), featured sexual and bawdy elements; _Back to the Future_ was considered too tame in comparison.[\[22\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesRushedPostPro-24)[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) Columbia put the project into [turnaround](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turnaround_(filmmaking) "Turnaround (filmmaking)") (a process allowing other studios to purchase the idea).[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11)[\[23\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201513-25) The script was rejected some forty times, sometimes multiple times by the same studios.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10) Reasons given included the concept being unappealing to contemporary rebellious youth[\[23\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201513-25) and the failures of other time travel films, such as _[The Final Countdown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Final_Countdown_(film) "The Final Countdown (film)")_ (1980) and _[Time Bandits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_Bandits "Time Bandits")_ (1981).[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11)[\[24\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Gizmodo11things-26) [Walt Disney Productions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures "Walt Disney Pictures") turned it down because they considered Marty's fighting off his future mother's advances too risqué for their brand.[\[22\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesRushedPostPro-24) The only supporter of the project was Spielberg, but with their previous collaborations considered relative failures, Gale and Zemeckis feared another misstep would suggest they could get work only through being friends with Spielberg.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)[\[22\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesRushedPostPro-24)

Zemeckis accepted the next project offered to him, _[Romancing the Stone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romancing_the_Stone "Romancing the Stone")_ (1984).[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HFPAOralHistory-12)[\[22\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesRushedPostPro-24)[\[25\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201514-27) Against expectations, the film was a significant success and gave Zemeckis enough credibility to return to _Back to the Future_.[\[c\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-29) Zemeckis held a grudge against the studios that had rejected the project and turned to Spielberg, who had set up his own production company, [Amblin Entertainment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amblin_Entertainment "Amblin Entertainment"), at [Universal Pictures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Pictures "Universal Pictures"), where Price now worked.[\[18\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ShortList-20)[\[27\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201516-30) Spielberg disliked Price because he had rejected _[E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E.T._the_Extra-Terrestrial "E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial")_ (1982) and demanded his involvement in _Back to the Future_ be minimal. [Sidney Sheinberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidney_Sheinberg "Sidney Sheinberg") installed himself as chief executive to oversee the studio's investment in the project.[\[28\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201517-31) Amblin executives [Kathleen Kennedy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kathleen_Kennedy_(producer) "Kathleen Kennedy (producer)") and [Frank Marshall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Marshall_(filmmaker) "Frank Marshall (filmmaker)") joined Spielberg as the film's [executive producers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_producers "Executive producers").[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11)[\[29\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VanityFairPowerful-32)

However, rights to _Back to the Future_ remained with Columbia Pictures. Price's successor at Columbia, [Guy McElwaine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guy_McElwaine "Guy McElwaine"), was developing a satire of the Universal-owned noir film _[Double Indemnity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_Indemnity "Double Indemnity")_ (1944) called _[Big Trouble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_Trouble_(1986_film) "Big Trouble (1986 film)")_ (1986). Its similarities to _Double Indemnity_ meant the studio would violate Universal's copyright. With production imminent, McElwaine asked for the rights from Price; in exchange, Price obtained the rights to _Back to the Future_.[\[30\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DeadlinePrice-33)

Sheinberg suggested modifications to the film, including changing the title to _Space Man from Pluto_, believing _Back to the Future_ would not resonate with audiences.[\[19\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-CNNGaleInterview-21)[\[31\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Radio_Times_30_August_2016-34) Gale and Zemeckis did not know how to reject Sheinberg's suggestions without risking his ire. Spielberg intervened, sending Sheinberg a memo reading: "Hi Sid, thanks for your most humorous memo, we all got a big laugh out of it, keep 'em coming." Spielberg knew Sheinberg would be too embarrassed to admit his memo was to be taken seriously.[\[18\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ShortList-20)[\[31\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Radio_Times_30_August_2016-34) Sheinberg later claimed the story was "bullshit".[\[32\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015111-35) Sheinberg also wanted to change the name of Marty's mother from Meg to Lorraine (a tribute to his wife [Lorraine Gary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorraine_Gary "Lorraine Gary")), and rename Professor Brown to Doc Brown because he considered it more accessible.[\[19\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-CNNGaleInterview-21)[\[33\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201518-36) The third draft was completed by July 1984.[\[33\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201518-36) The lengthy development allowed Gale and Zemeckis to refine the script's jokes, especially ones that had become dated since 1980.[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesGaleJul85-13) The joke about former actor [Ronald Reagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan "Ronald Reagan") becoming [President of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_the_United_States "President of the United States") remained following his re-election in [1984](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984_United_States_presidential_election "1984 United States presidential election").[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesGaleJul85-13)

### Casting

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: Casting")\]

[![portrait of Eric Stoltz](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Eric_Stoltz-2009_cropped.jpg/250px-Eric_Stoltz-2009_cropped.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Eric_Stoltz-2009_cropped.jpg) [Eric Stoltz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Stoltz "Eric Stoltz") (pictured in 2009) was cast as Marty McFly and spent several weeks filming _Back to the Future_ before the role was re-cast.

[Michael J. Fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_J._Fox "Michael J. Fox") was the first choice to portray Marty McFly. Gale and Zemeckis believed his acting timing in the [NBC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC "NBC") sitcom _[Family Ties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_Ties "Family Ties")_ (1982–1989) as the sophisticated [Alex P. Keaton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_P._Keaton "Alex P. Keaton") could be translated to Marty's clumsiness.[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HFPAOralHistory-12)[\[34\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesFoxInterview-37) Spielberg asked the show's producer [Gary David Goldberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gary_David_Goldberg "Gary David Goldberg") to have Fox read the script. Concerned Fox's absence would damage _Family Ties_' success, especially with fellow star [Meredith Baxter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meredith_Baxter "Meredith Baxter") on [maternity leave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parental_leave "Parental leave"), Goldberg did not give Fox the script.[\[35\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines20154%E2%80%935-38) Other young stars were considered, including: [John Cusack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Cusack "John Cusack"), [C. Thomas Howell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C._Thomas_Howell "C. Thomas Howell"), [Johnny Depp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johnny_Depp "Johnny Depp"), [Ralph Macchio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ralph_Macchio "Ralph Macchio"), [Charlie Sheen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie_Sheen "Charlie Sheen"), [Jon Cryer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jon_Cryer "Jon Cryer"), [Ben Stiller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Stiller "Ben Stiller"), [Peter DeLuise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_DeLuise "Peter DeLuise"), [Billy Zane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billy_Zane "Billy Zane"), [George Newbern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Newbern "George Newbern"), [Robert Downey Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Downey_Jr. "Robert Downey Jr."), [Christopher Collet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Collet "Christopher Collet"), [Matthew Modine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthew_Modine "Matthew Modine"), and [Corey Hart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corey_Hart_(singer) "Corey Hart (singer)") (who declined to audition).[\[d\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-43) Howell was the frontrunner,[\[37\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201519-40) but Sheinberg preferred [Eric Stoltz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Stoltz "Eric Stoltz"), who had impressed with his portrayal of [Rocky Dennis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roy_L._Dennis "Roy L. Dennis") in an early screening of the drama film _[Mask](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mask_(1985_film) "Mask (1985 film)")_ (1985).[\[40\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201520-44)[\[38\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureLostRoles-41) With the filming date approaching, Zemeckis opted for Stoltz.[\[40\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201520-44) Sheinberg promised that if Stoltz did not work out, they could reshoot the film.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) The character's name was derived from _Used Cars_ production assistant Marty Casella. Zemeckis suggested McFly because it sounded "All-American".[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)

Among others, [Jeff Goldblum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeff_Goldblum "Jeff Goldblum"), [John Lithgow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Lithgow "John Lithgow"), [Dudley Moore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dudley_Moore "Dudley Moore"), [Ron Silver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ron_Silver "Ron Silver"), [Robin Williams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robin_Williams "Robin Williams"), [John Cleese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Cleese "John Cleese"), [Mandy Patinkin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandy_Patinkin "Mandy Patinkin"), [Gene Hackman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene_Hackman "Gene Hackman"), [James Woods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Woods "James Woods"), and [Mark Mothersbaugh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Mothersbaugh "Mark Mothersbaugh") were considered for the role of Doc Brown.[\[e\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-47) Producer [Neil Canton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_Canton "Neil Canton") suggested Lithgow, having worked with him and [Christopher Lloyd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Lloyd "Christopher Lloyd") on _[Buckaroo Banzai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Buckaroo_Banzai_Across_the_8th_Dimension "The Adventures of Buckaroo Banzai Across the 8th Dimension")_ (1984). Lithgow was unavailable, and the role was offered to Lloyd. He was reluctant to join the production until a friend encouraged him to take the part.[\[43\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ScreenRangDocB-48) [Albert Einstein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Einstein "Albert Einstein") and conductor [Leopold Stokowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leopold_Stokowski "Leopold Stokowski") inspired Lloyd's wild, white hair.[\[44\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Seattle_times-49) Lloyd affected a hunched posture to lower his 6 feet 1 inch (1.85 meters) height closer to the 5 feet 5 inches (1.65 m) tall Fox.[\[38\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureLostRoles-41)

The filmmakers became aware of [Lea Thompson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lea_Thompson "Lea Thompson") while researching Stoltz in the comedy-drama _[The Wild Life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Wild_Life_(film) "The Wild Life (film)")_ (1984).[\[45\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AVClubThompson-50) [Crispin Glover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crispin_Glover "Crispin Glover") used many of his own mannerisms in portraying George McFly. Gale described his performance as "nuts", and Zemeckis was reportedly unhappy with Glover's performance choices, instructing him to be more restrained as the older George.[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)[\[46\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AVClubGlover-51) Glover lost his voice during filming and later dubbed in some lines.[\[8\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ShortlistDudley-9) DeLuise, Zane, [Tim Robbins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tim_Robbins "Tim Robbins"), and [J. J. Cohen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._J._Cohen "J. J. Cohen") were considered to play Biff Tannen.[\[8\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ShortlistDudley-9)[\[47\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-JJCohen-52)[\[48\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-YahoOCast-53) Cohen was not considered intimidating enough against Stoltz, and the role went to [ThomasF. Wilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_F._Wilson "Thomas F. Wilson"), his first feature starring role.[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStoltz-54)[\[50\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-JJCohen2-55) Zane and Cohen were cast as Biff's minions Match and Skinhead instead.[\[47\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-JJCohen-52)[\[51\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-USATodayThings-56) Tannen's name was taken from Universal Studios executive [Ned Tanen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ned_Tanen "Ned Tanen"), who had been unpleasant with Gale and Zemeckis.[\[8\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ShortlistDudley-9)

[Melora Hardin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melora_Hardin "Melora Hardin") was cast as Jennifer Parker on a two-film contract. After Stoltz's replacement, the crew were polled about Hardin being taller than Fox; the female crew overwhelmingly voted Marty should not be shorter than his girlfriend.[\[38\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureLostRoles-41)[\[52\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-WiredHardin-57)[\[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201542%E2%80%9343-58) Hardin was replaced by [Claudia Wells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claudia_Wells "Claudia Wells"), who had previously declined the role because of her commitment to the short-lived television series _[Off the Rack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Off_the_Rack "Off the Rack")_ (1984).[\[38\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureLostRoles-41)[\[52\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-WiredHardin-57)[\[54\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201543-59) Actresses [Kyra Sedgwick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyra_Sedgwick "Kyra Sedgwick") and [Jill Schoelen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jill_Schoelen "Jill Schoelen") were also considered; Schoelen was told she looked too "exotic" and not sufficiently All-American.[\[55\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FangoriaSchoelen-60)[\[56\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-PeopleSedgwick-61) Doc Brown's pet, a dog named Einstein, was originally scripted as a [chimpanzee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chimpanzee "Chimpanzee") named Shemp. Sheinberg insisted films featuring chimps never did well.[\[8\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ShortlistDudley-9)[\[24\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Gizmodo11things-26) [James Tolkan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Tolkan "James Tolkan") was the first choice for Principal Strickland after Zemeckis saw him in the crime drama _[Prince of the City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_of_the_City "Prince of the City")_ (1981).[\[57\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201584,_85-62) Singer and soundtrack contributor [Huey Lewis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huey_Lewis "Huey Lewis") cameos as a Battle of the Bands judge. Lewis agreed to appear as long as he was uncredited and could wear a disguise.[\[7\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-USATodayLewis-8) Gale cameos as the hand in the radiation suit tapping the DeLorean time display.[\[58\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-THRGaleCameo-63)

### Filming with Stoltz

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: Filming with Stoltz")\]

[![bungalow with an attached garage, with a tower and power lines in the background](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/The_house_of_M%D1%81Fly_family_02.jpg/250px-The_house_of_M%D1%81Fly_family_02.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_house_of_M%D1%81Fly_family_02.jpg) A house in [Arleta, Los Angeles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arleta,_Los_Angeles "Arleta, Los Angeles"), served as the McFlys' home.

[Principal photography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principal_photography "Principal photography") began on November26, 1984, on a 14-week schedule set to conclude on February28, 1985, with an estimated $14million budget.[\[59\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKlastorinAtamaniuk201547,_61-64)[\[60\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines20152,_32-65) Filming took place mainly at the [Universal Studios Lot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Studios_Lot "Universal Studios Lot") and on location in [California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California "California").[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15) [Dean Cundey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dean_Cundey "Dean Cundey") served as the cinematographer; he and Zemeckis had collaborated on _Romancing the Stone_.[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15) Editor [Arthur Schmidt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Schmidt_(film_editor) "Arthur Schmidt (film editor)") was hired after Zemeckis saw his work on _[Firstborn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Firstborn_(1984_film) "Firstborn (1984 film)")_ (1984); Schmidt recommended hiring [Harry Keramidas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Keramidas "Harry Keramidas") as co-editor.[\[61\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines20152%E2%80%933,_23-66) Frank Marshall also served as a second unit director.[\[62\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201587-67)

Owing to the tight schedule, editing occurred concurrently with filming.[\[63\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines20151%E2%80%932-68) On December30, 1984, Zemeckis reviewed the existing scenes with Schmidt and Keramidas.[\[64\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201521%E2%80%9322,_27-69) Zemeckis was reluctant to review the footage because he would be self-critical,[\[65\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201521,_22-70) but he believed Stoltz's acting was not working and had already listed several scenes he wanted to reshoot.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)[\[65\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201521,_22-70) Zemeckis called in Gale and the producers to show them the footage; they agreed Stoltz was not right for the part.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10) Stoltz was performing the role with an intense and serious tone, not the " [screwball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Screwball_comedy "Screwball comedy")" energy they desired.[\[34\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesFoxInterview-37)[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStoltz-54) Gale characterized Stoltz as a good actor in the wrong role.[\[66\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTDateMovedUp-71)

Stoltz utilized [method acting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_acting "Method acting") and stayed in character as Marty when not filming, refusing to answer to his own name. This resulted in feuding with some of the cast and crew, including Wilson. Stoltz put his full strength into pushing Wilson rather than imitating doing so, despite Wilson's protests.[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStoltz-54) Spielberg said Zemeckis needed a replacement in place before firing Stoltz, or he risked the production being canceled.[\[67\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201528%E2%80%9329-72) Zemeckis and the producers asked Sheinberg for permission to do whatever was necessary to accommodate Fox's participation;[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStoltz-54) Spielberg made another call to Goldberg. On January3, 1985, Goldberg told Fox about withholding the _Back to the Future_ script from him, and the filmmakers wanted to know if he was interested. Baxter had returned to the show, and they could be more flexible with Fox as long as _Family Ties_ took priority. Fox agreed to join without reading the script.[\[68\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201531%E2%80%9333-73) The transition could not take place immediately and filming continued with Stoltz in the lead role, unaware he was to be replaced.[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStoltz-54)

On January 10, 1985, Zemeckis informed Stoltz that he was being fired.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11)[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStoltz-54)[\[69\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201535%E2%80%9336-74) Zemeckis described it as "the hardest meeting I've ever had in my life and it was all my fault. I broke \[Stoltz's\] heart."[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) Stoltz was reported to have told his makeup artist he was not a [comedian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comedian "Comedian") and did not understand why he was cast.[\[70\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201525%E2%80%9326-75) The producers informed the principal cast and the rest of the crew much of the film would be re-shot.[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStoltz-54)[\[71\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKlastorinAtamaniuk201561,_66-76) Cundey said most of the crew saw Stoltz's removal as "good news".[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15) Crew members later said there were obvious signs Stoltz would be replaced; the set designers were told not to change the 1955 set, and a scene involving a discussion between Marty and Doc was filmed showing only Doc.[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStoltz-54) Stoltz had shot numerous key scenes including Marty traveling to 1955 in the DeLorean, its breaking down as he prepares to return to 1985, and his final scene was Marty's return to 1985.[\[46\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AVClubGlover-51)[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStoltz-54) Filming fell behind schedule, with 34days of filming lost and an additional cost of $3.5–$4.0million, including Stoltz receiving his salary in full.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11)[\[66\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTDateMovedUp-71)[\[72\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201533,_52-77) Universal Pictures' marketing team was tasked with mitigating the negative publicity from a project replacing its main star.[\[73\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201552-78)

### Filming with Fox

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Filming with Fox")\]

[![the courthouse with its clock tower](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Court_house_from_Back_to_the_Future_films.jpg/250px-Court_house_from_Back_to_the_Future_films.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Court_house_from_Back_to_the_Future_films.jpg) The [Hill Valley town square](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Courthouse_Square "Courthouse Square") and clock tower were a set built on the [Universal Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Studios_Hollywood "Universal Studios Hollywood")' [backlot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backlot "Backlot").

Fox's first day on set was January15, 1985.[\[74\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201541,_43%E2%80%9344-79) He filmed _Family Ties_ during the day before traveling to the _Back to the Future_ filming location. Often, he would not return home until early the following morning, and on weekends, the schedule was pushed back further as _Family Ties_ was filmed in front of a live audience.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11)[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)[\[34\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesFoxInterview-37) The [teamster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teamster "Teamster") drivers entrusted with dropping off Fox at home often had to carry the actor to bed.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) This continued until April, when _Family Ties_ finished filming.[\[75\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015103%E2%80%93104-80) Gale said Fox's youth meant he could cope with less sleep than usual;[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15) Fox described it as exhausting, but worth the effort.[\[34\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesFoxInterview-37) Further into the filming schedule, Fox was energetic during his scenes but struggled to stay awake off set. He ad-libbed some lines when he forgot the intended dialogue,[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)[\[76\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015114-81) and recalled looking for a camcorder on the _Family Ties_ set, before realizing it was a prop on _Back to the Future_.[\[76\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015114-81) He also had to learn to mimic playing the guitar and choreographed skateboarding routines taught by [Per Welinder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Per_Welinder "Per Welinder") and Bob Schmelzer.[\[77\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-CBRSkateboard-82)

To compensate for his conflicting schedules and reduce production costs, some scenes involving Marty were shot without Fox, who filmed his part separately.[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HFPAOralHistory-12)[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15) Re-shooting scenes allowed the filmmakers to identify problems and implement new ideas. To avoid building an additional classroom set, the opening pan across the array of clocks in Doc Brown's laboratory replaced an opening scene where Marty sets off a fire alarm to get out of detention.[\[17\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ColliderDifferences2020-18)[\[78\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201550-83) The height differences between Stoltz and Fox necessitated other changes, such as a scene of Fox teaching George how to punch because Fox could not reach the necessary prop.[\[79\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201551-84) According to Gale, once Fox replaced Stoltz, the atmosphere on set improved.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) Thompson anecdotally said while Stoltz ate lunch alone in his trailer, Fox ate lunch with the cast and crew.[\[80\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201547-85)

The production used many locations in and around [Los Angeles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles"). The [clock tower and town square](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Courthouse_Square "Courthouse Square") are structures on the [Universal Studios Lot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Studios_Lot "Universal Studios Lot") in [Universal City, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_City,_California "Universal City, California").[\[81\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ClockTower-86)[\[82\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Curbed-87) When filmed from below, Lloyd was positioned on a recreation of the clock tower, but when filmed from above, Lloyd stood atop the tower itself.[\[83\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198564-88) Production designer [Lawrence G. Paull](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lawrence_G._Paull "Lawrence G. Paull") insisted on using the Universal backlot sets because of the difficulties and costs involved in making an on-location area look 1955-appropriate.[\[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015143-89) [Whittier High School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whittier_High_School "Whittier High School") in the city of [Whittier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whittier,_California "Whittier, California") is the Hill Valley high school. Marty's home and the surrounding Lyon estates are in [Arleta, Los Angeles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arleta,_Los_Angeles "Arleta, Los Angeles"). Several of the residential locations were filmed in Pasadena: Lorraine's and George's 1955 homes, and Doc Brown's 1955 home. (Its exterior is the [Gamble House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamble_House_(Pasadena,_California) "Gamble House (Pasadena, California)"); interiors were shot at the historic [Blacker House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blacker_House "Blacker House").)[\[82\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Curbed-87) [Puente Hills Mall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puente_Hills_Mall "Puente Hills Mall") in [City of Industry, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City_of_Industry,_California "City of Industry, California") serves as the Twin Pines mall, which later becomes the Lone Pine mall after Marty knocks over one of the trees at Twin Pines ranch in 1955, which was filmed at the Walt Disney Studios-owned [Golden Oak Ranch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Oak_Ranch "Golden Oak Ranch") in [Newhall, Santa Clarita, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newhall,_Santa_Clarita,_California "Newhall, Santa Clarita, California").[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStoltz-54)[\[82\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Curbed-87) Other locations include the basement of the [Hollywood United Methodist Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood_United_Methodist_Church "Hollywood United Methodist Church") where the school dance was filmed, and [Griffith Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Griffith_Park "Griffith Park"), where Marty begins his drive to the courthouse to return to 1985, passing by a lamp post outside the [Greek Theatre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_Theatre_(Los_Angeles) "Greek Theatre (Los Angeles)").[\[82\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Curbed-87)

Filming [concluded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wrap_(filmmaking) "Wrap (filmmaking)") after 107 days on April26, 1985. The final day of filming included [pick-up](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pick-up_(filmmaking) "Pick-up (filmmaking)") shots of Marty and Einstein the dog in the DeLorean.[\[75\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015103%E2%80%93104-80)

### Post-production

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Post-production")\]

[![the Century 22 Theater in San Jose where the film was test screened](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Century_Domes%2C_San_Jose_%282773755882%29.jpg/250px-Century_Domes%2C_San_Jose_%282773755882%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Century_Domes,_San_Jose_(2773755882).jpg) A rough cut of the film was test screened for audiences at [Century 22](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Century_Theatres "Century Theatres") theater in [San Jose, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Jose,_California "San Jose, California"), only three weeks after filming concluded.

Arthur F. Repola served as the post-production supervisor, but he became responsible for many aspects outside his role, including budgets, storyboarding, and general problem-solving. Those roles belonged to Kennedy and Marshall, but both were occupied on other films.[\[85\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198540-90) Schmidt found editing the film difficult because he had to imagine where the special effects would later be added; there was no time or budget to re-edit afterward.[\[86\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ABoutSchmidt-91)

A [rough version of the movie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workprint "Workprint") was cut together for a [test screening](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Test_screening "Test screening") at the [Century 22](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Century_Theatres "Century Theatres") theater in [San Jose, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Jose,_California "San Jose, California"), in mid-May 1985, just three weeks after filming concluded. The audience was seemingly uninterested at the exposition-heavy opening but became engaged after the DeLorean appeared.[\[87\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015104,_106%E2%80%93107-92) At a test screening in [Long Beach, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_Beach,_California "Long Beach, California"), 94% of the audience responded they would recommend the film; 99% rated it very good or excellent.[\[22\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesRushedPostPro-24) Gale said there was some concern when Doc's dog Einstein was sent through time, as the audience believed he had been killed.[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15) But Gale said when they came to the cafe scene where Marty sees his father, the audience "got it". The film was re-cut and screened again at the [Alfred Hitchcock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Hitchcock "Alfred Hitchcock") theater at Universal Studios for executives, including Sheinberg.[\[88\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015108%E2%80%93109-93) He was so impressed he moved the scheduled release date forward to July3, 1985, to give it more time in theaters during the peak summer season.[\[66\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTDateMovedUp-71) The new date reduced the post-production schedule to just nine weeks for special effects and editing.[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)[\[66\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTDateMovedUp-71) Zemeckis spent much of June rushing to finish the film.[\[22\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesRushedPostPro-24)

Deleted scenes include: Doc looking at an issue of _[Playboy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Playboy "Playboy")_, remarking the future looks better; a scene of 1985 George being coerced into buying a large amount of peanut brittle from a young girl;[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)[\[89\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOG88things-94) a scene of young George trapped in a phone booth by the man who interrupts his dance with Lorraine;[\[90\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015108-95) and the scene of Marty pretending to be "Darth Vader", which was shortened.[\[89\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOG88things-94) Zemeckis considered cutting the " [JohnnyB. Goode](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johnny_B._Goode "Johnny B. Goode")" performance because it did not advance the story, but test audiences reacted well to it.[\[91\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015107%E2%80%93108-96) There is a dispute if a shot of Stoltz's hand is in the finished film in the scene where Marty punches Biff. Gale noted it is impossible to tell without checking the original film negative, which would risk damaging it.[\[51\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-USATodayThings-56)[\[92\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DigitalSpyHand-97) The final 116‑minute cut was completed on June 23, 1985.[\[93\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015109-98)[\[94\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BBFC-99) Universal Studios took out a full-page advertisement in _[Variety](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variety_(magazine) "Variety (magazine)")_ magazine, thanking the post-production crew for completing their work on time.[\[93\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015109-98) The final budget was $19million.[\[95\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015132-100)[\[96\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BomBOSummary-101)

### Music

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Music")\]

Main article: [_Back to the Future_ (soundtrack)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_(soundtrack) "Back to the Future (soundtrack)")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/60px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png)

[_Alan Silvestri – Back to the Future_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Back_to_the_Future_Theme_by_Alan_Silvestri.mp3 "File:Back to the Future Theme by Alan Silvestri.mp3")

[Play audio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Back_to_the_Future_Theme_by_Alan_Silvestri.mp3 "Play audio") Duration: 20 seconds.0:20

Alan Silvestri wanted to create a "heroic" theme that could be recognizable from only a few notes.

* * *

_Problems playing this file? See [media help](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Media "Help:Media")._

[Alan Silvestri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Silvestri "Alan Silvestri") composed the score for _Back to the Future_; he had worked with Zemeckis on _Romancing the Stone_. The only direction Zemeckis gave him was "it's got to be big". Silvestri used an orchestral score to create a sound that contrasted with the small-town setting and the significant time-changing events occurring within it. He wanted a heroic theme that would be instantly recognizable.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11)

Huey Lewis was approached to write a theme song for the film; he was coming off the success of his recent album _[Sports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sports_(Huey_Lewis_and_the_News_album) "Sports (Huey Lewis and the News album)")_. He met with Gale, Spielberg, and Zemeckis, who intended that [Huey Lewis and the News](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huey_Lewis_and_the_News "Huey Lewis and the News") be Marty's favorite band. Though flattered, Lewis did not want to participate because he did not know how to write film songs and did not want to write one called "Back to the Future". Zemeckis assured Lewis he could write any song he wanted. Lewis agreed to submit the next song he wrote, which was " [The Power of Love](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Power_of_Love_(Huey_Lewis_and_the_News_song) "The Power of Love (Huey Lewis and the News song)")".[\[7\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-USATodayLewis-8) Lewis maintains "Power of Love" was his first submission, but Zemeckis recalled a different first song that was rejected.[\[97\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201596-102)[\[98\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AFIGB-103) Lewis later acquiesced to Zemeckis's request for a second song, " [Back in Time](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_in_Time_(Huey_Lewis_and_the_News_song) "Back in Time (Huey Lewis and the News song)")".[\[7\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-USATodayLewis-8)

Musician [Eddie Van Halen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddie_Van_Halen "Eddie Van Halen") performed the guitar riff Marty (dressed as "Darth Vader") uses to wake George. The filmmakers wanted to use [Van Halen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Van_Halen "Van Halen")'s music, but the band refused to take part, so Eddie took part on his own. [Mark Campbell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jack_Mack_and_the_Heart_Attack "Jack Mack and the Heart Attack") provided Marty's singing voice, but did not receive credit, as the filmmakers wanted to pretend Fox was singing. When music supervisor [Bones Howe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bones_Howe "Bones Howe") learned of this, he secured Campbell a small percentage of the soundtrack revenue as compensation.[\[89\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOG88things-94)[\[99\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201588-104) [Paul Hanson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Hanson_(guitarist) "Paul Hanson (guitarist)") taught Fox how to use a guitar to play " [Johnny B. Goode](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johnny_B._Goode "Johnny B. Goode")", and choreographer Brad Jeffries spent four weeks teaching Fox to replicate various rock star moves popularized by artists like [Pete Townshend](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Townshend "Pete Townshend"), [Jimi Hendrix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix "Jimi Hendrix"), and Chuck Berry.[\[100\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EmpireGuitar-105)[\[101\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201590-106) Berry withheld permission to use "Johnny B. Goode" until the day before filming, receiving $50,000 for the rights.[\[102\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TelegraphThings-107) Harry WatersJr. provided the vocals on " [Earth Angel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_Angel "Earth Angel")".[\[103\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201592%E2%80%9393-108)

## Design

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Design")\]

### Special effects

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Special effects")\]

[Industrial Light & Magic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic "Industrial Light & Magic") (ILM) developed the film's special effects under the supervision of [Ken Ralston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ken_Ralston "Ken Ralston") and [Kevin Pike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Pike "Kevin Pike").[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ASCILM-4)[\[104\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BTTFWebsite-109) It contains approximately 27–32 special effects shots, compared to the 300 such shots typical in contemporaneous higher-budget films.[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ASCILM-4)[\[8\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ShortlistDudley-9)[\[85\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198540-90) Despite working simultaneously on _[The Goonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Goonies "The Goonies")_ and _[Cocoon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cocoon_(film) "Cocoon (film)")_, Ralston took on the additional project because it required relatively few effects, and he wanted to realize the planned ending of Marty driving the time machine into a nuclear explosion.[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ASCILM-4)[\[85\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198540-90) The team had a nine-and-a-half-week schedule, reduced to less than nine once Universal Pictures moved up the release date. ILM was working on _Back to the Future_ up to the moment it had to be handed over to print the theatrical film reels.[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ASCILM-4)[\[105\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198540,_59-110)

The tight schedule affected the special effects' quality. Ralston was disappointed by the scene where Marty's hand fades away as his future is altered. Fox was filmed separately from his hand and the two were [composited](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compositing "Compositing") together; the hand was filmed with a wide-angle lens, making it appear too large, and it had to be scaled down. Zemeckis wanted a subtle fade, but it resulted in a small circle of the hand fading away and there was no time to fix it.[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ASCILM-4)[\[106\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198563-111) In the same scene, Marty and his siblings fade away from a photo. ILM found it difficult to fade the photo's individual aspects, especially as it was moving on the neck of a guitar. A replica of the guitar neck was constructed at four times the normal size; the guitar strings were made of cable up to a quarter-inch thick. An 11-by-14 aluminum plate was attached to hold the enlarged photograph. ILM used a version of the photo without Marty or his siblings and individually pasted each character into the photo. When this failed, four different photos were used: one containing the background, and one for each McFly sibling. A mechanical camera cycled through each photo and printed it to the film.[\[106\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198563-111) The enlarged guitar was moved around to add to the realism.[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ASCILM-4)

The original nuclear explosion ending was considered too complicated and expensive, with an estimated cost of $1million.[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ASCILM-4)[\[15\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SlashFilmFridge-16)[\[17\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ColliderDifferences2020-18) Art director [Andrew Probert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Probert "Andrew Probert") storyboarded the scene, which would have been created using sets and [miniatures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scale_model "Scale model").[\[15\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SlashFilmFridge-16)[\[106\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198563-111) With the ending moved to the clock tower, ILM researched storms to achieve the right aesthetic.[\[106\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198563-111) Clouds were constructed from [polyester fiberfill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polyester_Fiberfill "Polyester Fiberfill"), suspended in a net, and filmed from above while Ralston shone a powerful light from below.[\[83\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198564-88) He used a [rheostat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potentiometer#Rheostat "Potentiometer") to rapidly change the lights' intensity to imitate lightning.[\[83\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198564-88)

Developed by [Wes Takahashi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wes_Takahashi "Wes Takahashi")'s animation department, the lightning bolt that strikes the clock tower was described as "the largest bolt of lightning in cinematic history". It was intended to originate in the distance and move closer, but the footage was filmed too close to the tower and there was insufficient space between it and the top of the frame.[\[107\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FXGuide-112) There was also an issue with showing the bolt onscreen for too long as it made it more obviously animated.[\[83\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198564-88)[\[107\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FXGuide-112) The frame count was reduced, but the bolt did not look chaotic enough.[\[83\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198564-88) Zemeckis picked out a single frame of the bolt in an "S"formation and asked that the effect focus on that shape and be reduced to twenty frames.[\[83\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198564-88)[\[107\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FXGuide-112) The bolt was drawn in black ink on white paper; diffusion effects and a glow were added by the optical department.[\[107\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FXGuide-112)

### The DeLorean time machine

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: The DeLorean time machine")\]

Main article: [DeLorean time machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DeLorean_time_machine "DeLorean time machine")

[![refer to caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Front_Side_Wings_Aloft.jpg/250px-Front_Side_Wings_Aloft.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Front_Side_Wings_Aloft.jpg) The [DeLorean time machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DeLorean_time_machine "DeLorean time machine") on display in 2021

The DeLorean was developed under the supervision of Lawrence Paull,[\[104\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BTTFWebsite-109) who designed it with artist [Ron Cobb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ron_Cobb "Ron Cobb") and illustrator [Andrew Probert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Probert "Andrew Probert").[\[24\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Gizmodo11things-26)[\[108\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198556-113) They intended for the vehicle to look fixed together from common parts.[\[104\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BTTFWebsite-109) The time machine was originally conceived as a stationary device; at one point it was a refrigerator.
