Spielberg vetoed the idea, concerned child viewers might attempt to climb into one.[\[15\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SlashFilmFridge-16) Zemeckis suggested the DeLorean because it offered mobility and a unique design; the gull-wing doors would appear like an alien [UFO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unidentified_flying_object "Unidentified flying object") to a 1950s family.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11)[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HFPAOralHistory-12) The [Ford Motor Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company "Ford Motor Company") offered $75,000 to use a [Ford Mustang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ford_Mustang "Ford Mustang") instead; Gale responded, "Doc Brown doesn't drive a fucking Mustang".[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) Michael Fink was hired as the art department liaison and tasked with realizing Cobb's sketches and overseeing the car's construction. He was recruited by Paull and Canton, who had worked with him on _[Blade Runner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blade_Runner "Blade Runner")_ (1982) and _Buckaroo Banzai_, respectively. Fink had a project lined up but agreed to help in the free weeks he had remaining.[\[104\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BTTFWebsite-109) Three DeLoreans used were purchased from a collector: one for stunts, one for special effects, and a more detailed [hero version](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prop#Hero "Prop") for close-up shots.[\[108\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198556-113)[\[109\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201563-114) They were unreliable and often broke down.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) 88 miles per hour (142 kilometers per hour) was chosen as the time travel speed because it was easy to remember and looked "cool" on the speedometer.[\[102\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TelegraphThings-107)

The flying DeLorean in the final scene used a combination of live-action footage, animation, and a 1:5 scale (approximately 33 inches (840 millimeters) long) model built by [Steve Gawley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Gawley "Steve Gawley") and the model shop crew.[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ASCILM-4)[\[110\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198566,_67-115)[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ASCILM-4) The act of the DeLorean traveling through time was called the 'time slice' effect. Zemeckis knew only that he wanted the transition to be violent. He described it as a " [Neanderthal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthal "Neanderthal") sitting on the hood of the DeLorean and chipping away the fabric of time in front of him".[\[107\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FXGuide-112) The effect is so quick as to be imperceptible. Zemeckis preferred this, as he did not want the audience to think too much about how everything worked.[\[111\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198562-116)

### Art direction and makeup

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Art direction and makeup")\]

[![refer to caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Drew_Struzan_%282012%29.jpg/250px-Drew_Struzan_%282012%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Drew_Struzan_(2012).jpg) Artist [Drew Struzan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drew_Struzan "Drew Struzan") in 2012. He designed the _Back to the Future_ theatrical release poster.

Actual brand names, such as [Texaco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texaco "Texaco"), were used to make the sets more realistic, and the producers mandated the inclusion of certain brands that had paid to appear in the film. An unidentified gas company offered a large sum to be included, but Paull used Texaco because it reminded him of a joke from _[The Milton Berle Show](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Milton_Berle_Show "The Milton Berle Show")_.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)[\[112\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015143%E2%80%93144-117) This choice led to some disputes, such as [Pepsi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepsi "Pepsi") parent company, [PepsiCo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PepsiCo "PepsiCo"), wanting to omit a joke about the [Tab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tab_(drink) "Tab (drink)") drink made by its rival [Coca-Cola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company "The Coca-Cola Company").[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10) Twenty clock wranglers were needed to synch up the many clocks in the opening scene, and [pulleys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulleys "Pulleys") were used to start them simultaneously.[\[102\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TelegraphThings-107) [Drew Struzan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drew_Struzan "Drew Struzan") produced the film's poster.[\[113\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Nerdistmerch-118) The producers hoped his in-demand poster artwork would generate further interest in the film.[\[114\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201553-119)

The film uses a stylized adaptation of the 1950s [aesthetics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aesthetics "Aesthetics"), closer to television show interpretations than an exact recreation. Modern technologies such as contemporary fabrics were used because the designers believed the fashions of the time were not interesting.[\[20\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesJun1985AttheMovies-22) To represent characters across three decades, the filmmakers did not want to have older actors stand in for the younger ones, believing the change would be obvious and distracting. Special effects artist [Ken Chase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ken_Chase_(make-up_artist) "Ken Chase (make-up artist)") performed makeup tests on the young actors to age them; initial results were discouraging. He created a prosthetic neck and a [bald cap](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bald_cap "Bald cap") with a receding hairline for Glover but considered them excessive. Chase found it difficult to balance aging the actors and retaining enough of their natural appearance to remain recognizable.[\[108\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198556-113)

Casts were made of the actors' faces, from which plaster molds were made. Chase sculpted more subtle effects over the plaster molds using latex. For Lorraine, he crafted jowls and eye bags, plus body padding to reflect her increased weight and alcohol abuse.[\[115\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198556,_59-120) Instead of a receding hairline, Chase changed the style of George's hair; he used prosthetics only to give him a less-defined jawline.[\[116\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198559-121) Biff's character changed more significantly because Chase wanted him to look "obnoxious"; he was fattened, given sideburns, and a [comb over](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comb_over "Comb over") hairstyle to hide a growing bald spot.[\[116\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198559-121) The prosthetics were combined with makeup and lighting to further age the characters.[\[108\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198556-113)

Chase found the work frustrating compared to his experiences with more fantastical prostheses that made it easier to hide defects.[\[108\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198556-113) The rubber latex did not reflect light the same way as natural skin, so Chase used a [stippling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stippling "Stippling") process (creating a pattern with small dots) to variegate the actors' faces to better conceal where the skin and prosthetics met;[\[116\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198559-121) close-up shots were avoided.[\[116\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198559-121) Doc's appearance was not altered significantly. Chase painted latex on Lloyd which, when removed, caused crinkles in the skin, onto which other elements, such as [liver spots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liver_spot "Liver spot") and shadows, were painted.[\[116\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPourroy198559-121)

## Release

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Release")\]

### Context

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Context")\]

See also: [1985 in film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985_in_film "1985 in film")

[![refer to caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Back-to-the-future-logo.svg/250px-Back-to-the-future-logo.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Back-to-the-future-logo.svg) The logo for _Back to the Future_

By June 1985, the theatrical industry had experienced a 14% decline in ticket sales over the previous year's $4billion record sales. The summer period (beginning the final week of May) had 45films scheduled for release, including _[Rambo: First Blood Part II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rambo:_First_Blood_Part_II "Rambo: First Blood Part II")_, _The Goonies_, _[Brewster's Millions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brewster%27s_Millions_(1985_film) "Brewster's Millions (1985 film)")_, _[Fletch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fletch_(film) "Fletch (film)")_, and the latest [James Bond](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Bond "James Bond") film _[A View to a Kill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_View_to_a_Kill "A View to a Kill")_.[\[117\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985June11-122) This 25% increase over the previous year's releases led to concerns among industry professionals the competition would divide audiences and limit financial returns, at a time when the average cost of making and marketing a film had increased to $14.5million and $7million, respectively.[\[117\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985June11-122) A higher budget to secure a popular, and thus profitable, cast was considered a suitable risk.[\[117\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985June11-122) Most films scheduled for release were aimed at younger audiences, focusing on fantasy and the supernatural. Reflecting the times, these fantasy elements often employed a technological source instead of a magical one.[\[118\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985PostMortemCanby-123) Only a few films, like _Cocoon_ and _[Prizzi's Honor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prizzi%27s_Honor "Prizzi's Honor")_, targeted adults.[\[119\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesSeptBOOverview-124)

Initially, _Back to the Future_ was scheduled to be released in May 1985,[\[120\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines20152-125) but was pushed back to June21, the earliest Zemeckis could have the film ready. The delay caused by Stoltz's replacement pushed the release back to July19, and later to August.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) Sheinberg moved the release date forward to July3, giving it an extra sixteen days of theatrical screen time during the industry's most profitable period of the year. The move offered about 100,000 extra screenings, together worth an estimated $40million. He said he also wanted to avoid the negative perception of films released later in the summer period; other [blockbuster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blockbuster_(entertainment) "Blockbuster (entertainment)") films were usually released early.[\[66\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTDateMovedUp-71) The change required renegotiations with theater owners to secure screens in an already-crowded marketplace. In some cities, it was legally required that exhibitors be shown a film before purchase; an unfinished cut of the film was shown to theater owners and young test audiences. They described it as lesser than _E.T.the Extra-Terrestrial_ or _[Ghostbusters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghostbusters "Ghostbusters")_, but still a guaranteed box office hit.[\[66\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTDateMovedUp-71) Fox was unavailable for promotional work because he was filming _[Family Ties Vacation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Family_Ties_episodes#Film_(1985) "List of Family Ties episodes")_ (1985) in London.[\[121\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015113-126)

### Box office

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Box office")\]

In the United States (U.S.) and Canada, _Back to the Future_ received a wide release on July3, 1985, ahead of the [Independence Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Independence_Day_(United_States) "Independence Day (United States)") holiday weekend.[\[6\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985July3Maslin-7)[\[122\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMDaily-127) The film earned $3.6million during the opening Wednesday and Thursday,[\[122\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMDaily-127) and a further $11.3million during its inaugural weekend from 1,420 theaters – an average of $7,853 per theater.[\[123\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMWeekends-128) _Back to the Future_ finished as the number one film of the weekend ahead of Western _[Pale Rider](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pale_Rider "Pale Rider")_ ($7million), in its second weekend, and _Rambo: First Blood PartII_ ($6.4million) in its seventh.[\[124\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMNAWeekendJul5to7-129) It retained the number one position in its second weekend with a further gross of $10.6million, ahead of the debuting action film _[Mad Max Beyond Thunderdome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mad_Max_Beyond_Thunderdome "Mad Max Beyond Thunderdome")_ ($7.8million) and _Cocoon_ ($5million),[\[125\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMNAWeekendJul12to14-130) and in its third weekend, ahead of the re-release of _E.T.the Extra-Terrestrial_ ($8.8million) and _Mad Max Beyond Thunderdome_ ($5.4million).[\[126\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BomNAWeekendJul19to21-131) Although it fell to number two in its fourth weekend, behind the debuting _[National Lampoon's European Vacation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Lampoon%27s_European_Vacation "National Lampoon's European Vacation")_ ($12.3million), _Back to the Future_ regained the number one position in its fifth weekend and remained there for the following eight weeks.[\[123\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMWeekends-128)[\[127\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesBOAug71985-132) Recalling the opening weeks, Gale said, "our second weekend was higher than our first weekend, which is indicative of great [word of mouth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Word_of_mouth "Word of mouth")."[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)

The film remained a steady success, earning $155million by October, surpassing _Rambo: First Blood PartII_'s $149million box office earnings to become the year's highest-grossing film.[\[128\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesOct4Summ-133)[\[119\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesSeptBOOverview-124) In total, _Back to the Future_ was the number one film for eleven of its twelve first weeks and remained in the top ten highest-grossing films for a total of twenty-four.[\[123\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMWeekends-128) By the end of its theatrical run, _Back to the Future_ earned an approximate box office gross of $210.6million,[\[96\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BomBOSummary-101)[\[f\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-134) making it the highest-grossing film of 1985, ahead of _Rambo: First Blood PartII_ ($150.4million), the sports drama _[Rocky IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rocky_IV "Rocky IV")_ ($127.9million), and the drama _[The Color Purple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Color_Purple_(1985_film) "The Color Purple (1985 film)")_ ($94.2million).[\[129\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheNumbersNA1985-135)[\[130\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMNA1985-136) [Box Office Mojo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Box_Office_Mojo "Box Office Mojo") estimated more than 59million tickets were sold.[\[131\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMTickets-137) Industry experts suggest that as of 1997 the [box office returns to the studio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Film_distribution "Film distribution") (minus the theaters' share) was $105.5million.[\[132\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VarietyRentals-138)[\[g\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-139)

The year was considered an unsuccessful one for film. Despite a record number of film releases, ticket sales were down 17% compared with 1984.[\[119\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesSeptBOOverview-124)[\[133\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985Review-140) Industry executives blamed the problem, in part, on a lack of originality,[\[134\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985July3-141) and a glut of youth-oriented films targeted at those under18.[\[119\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesSeptBOOverview-124)[\[135\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985Xmas-142) Only _Back to the Future_ and _Rambo: First Blood PartII_ were considered blockbusters, earning more than double the box office of _Cocoon_.[\[119\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesSeptBOOverview-124) Films offering escapism and pro-America themes also fared well.[\[135\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985Xmas-142) After years of poor performances, _Back to the Future_, alongside _Fletch_, _Brewster's Millions_, and _Mask_, reversed Universal Pictures' fortunes.[\[135\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985Xmas-142)[\[136\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesOctMovieGiant-143)

Outside the United States and Canada, the film earned a further estimated $170.5million,[\[137\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015115-144)[\[h\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-145) making it the third-highest-grossing film of the year, behind the romantic drama _[Out of Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Out_of_Africa_(film) "Out of Africa (film)")_ ($179.1million) and _RockyIV_ ($172.6million).[\[137\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015115-144) Cumulatively, _Back to the Future_ earned a worldwide gross of $381.1million, making it the highest-grossing film of 1985, ahead of _RockyIV_ ($300.5million) and _Rambo: First Blood PartII_ ($300.4million).[\[96\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BomBOSummary-101)[\[138\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheNumbers85Worldwide-146)[\[139\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Bom85Worldwide-147)[\[i\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-148) _Back to the Future_ has received several theatrical re-releases to celebrate anniversaries, including a remastered version screened in 2010. These releases have raised the film's worldwide total to $388.8million.[\[140\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HomeMediaIndy-149)[\[141\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMAllReleasesSum-150)

## Reception

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Reception")\]

### Critical response

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Critical response")\]

[![A photograph of Lea Thompson](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Lea_Thompson_by_Gregg_Bond_%282008%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Lea_Thompson_by_Gregg_Bond_%282008%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lea_Thompson_by_Gregg_Bond_(2008)_(cropped).jpg)

[![A photograph of Crispin Glover](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Crispin_Glover_2012_Shankbone.JPG/250px-Crispin_Glover_2012_Shankbone.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Crispin_Glover_2012_Shankbone.JPG)

[Lea Thompson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lea_Thompson "Lea Thompson") in 2008 (left) and [Crispin Glover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crispin_Glover "Crispin Glover") in 2012. Critics praised the central cast, including Fox, Lloyd, Thompson, and Glover.

_Back to the Future_ received generally positive reviews from critics.[\[142\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Uproxxreception-151)[\[143\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BBCReception-152)[\[144\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EWModernRecep-153) Most reviewers agreed _Back to the Future_ was among the year's most entertaining films, partly because of its focus on storytelling instead of pure spectacle.[\[145\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesMaslinSpielberg-154)[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevWaPo-155) [Paul Attanasio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Attanasio "Paul Attanasio") and [Gene Siskel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene_Siskel "Gene Siskel") argued that while _Back to the Future_ appeared to be "everything wrong" with youth-targeted films, it successfully subverted expectations by focusing on a relatable narrative with an emotional core, and employed irreverent, good-natured humor. They, alongside [Richard Corliss](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Corliss "Richard Corliss"), agreed that it would endure because it offered something for children and adults.[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevWaPo-155)[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevTimeOut-156)[\[148\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevSiskel-157) Some reviewers, such as Corliss and [Leonard Maltin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonard_Maltin "Leonard Maltin") agreed that the exposition-heavy opening was _Back to the Future_'s weakest part, but led into a stronger half filled with "wit", "wonder", "comic epiphany", and original ideas.[\[4\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevVariety-5)[\[142\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Uproxxreception-151)[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevTimeOut-156)

[Dave Kehr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Kehr "Dave Kehr") remarked that Gale and Zemeckis were among the first generation of filmmakers openly influenced by growing up on televised entertainment, and their inspirations are evident throughout. _The Hollywood Reporter_ said that despite Spielberg's producer role, it was Zemeckis's vision, being more subtle, gentler, and "less noisy".[\[149\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevDaveKehr-158)[\[150\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevTHR-159) Some reviewers compared it favorably to the 1946 fantasy drama _[It's a Wonderful Life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/It%27s_a_Wonderful_Life "It's a Wonderful Life")_, which offered a similar premise of a central character changing his future. [Roger Ebert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Ebert "Roger Ebert") said the film offered humanity, charm, humor, and many surprises that were among its "greatest pleasures".[\[4\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevVariety-5)[\[150\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevTHR-159)[\[151\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevRogerEbert-160) [Sheila Benson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheila_Benson "Sheila Benson") was more critical; she found _Back to the Future_ to be overproduced and underdeveloped, featuring a hollow ending focused on materialistic rewards and lacking tension because Marty's success never seemed in doubt. Siskel countered that the tension came from defying the expectations of a typical time travel film by making the past mutable and the future uncertain.[\[148\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevSiskel-157)[\[152\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LATimesReview-161) [Paul Attanasio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Attanasio "Paul Attanasio") criticized some aspects that seemed to be "mechanically" designed to create the broadest audience appeal.[\[145\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesMaslinSpielberg-154)[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevWaPo-155)

The cast performances were generally well received, particularly those of Fox, Lloyd, Thompson, and Glover.[\[118\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985PostMortemCanby-123)[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevWaPo-155)[\[150\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevTHR-159) Reviewers consistently praised Fox's "appealing" performance, although some believed Lloyd's performance outshone the rest.[\[j\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-162) Kehr and Attanasio considered his uncontrolled performance and unique "intensity" a tribute to mad scientist characters, portrayed by the likes of [Sid Caesar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sid_Caesar "Sid Caesar") and [John Belushi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Belushi "John Belushi"), while creating the definitive scientist archetype for modern audiences.[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevWaPo-155)[\[149\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevDaveKehr-158)[\[150\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevTHR-159) In contrast, [Vincent Canby](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vincent_Canby "Vincent Canby") and _Variety_'s review said that Thompson's "deceptively passionate" performance and Glover's bumbling-to-confident character provided _Back to the Future_'s standout performances.[\[4\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevVariety-5)[\[118\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985PostMortemCanby-123) Some reviewers considered the use of Libyan terrorists, an actual fear at the time, to be in poor taste.[\[150\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevTHR-159)[\[152\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LATimesReview-161)

Audiences polled by [CinemaScore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CinemaScore "CinemaScore") gave the film an average grade of "A" on an A+ to F scale.[\[153\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-163)

### Accolades

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Accolades")\]

_Back to the Future_ received four nominations at the [43rd Golden Globe Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/43rd_Golden_Globe_Awards "43rd Golden Globe Awards"), for [Best Motion Picture (Musical or Comedy)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Motion_Picture_%E2%80%93_Musical_or_Comedy "Golden Globe Award for Best Motion Picture – Musical or Comedy"), [Best Actor in a Motion Picture (Musical or Comedy)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actor_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Musical_or_Comedy "Golden Globe Award for Best Actor – Motion Picture Musical or Comedy") (Fox), [Best Original Song](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Original_Song "Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song") ("The Power of Love"), and [Best Screenplay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Screenplay "Golden Globe Award for Best Screenplay") (Gale and Zemeckis).[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HFPAOralHistory-12)[\[154\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-GoldenGlobes86-164) The film was also named Favorite Motion Picture at the [12th People's Choice Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/12th_People%27s_Choice_Awards "12th People's Choice Awards").[\[155\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEN%C3%AD_Fhlainn20142-165) At the [1986 Academy Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/58th_Academy_Awards "58th Academy Awards"), _Back to the Future_ received one award for [Best Sound Effects Editing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Editing "Academy Award for Best Sound Editing") ( [CharlesL. Campbell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_L._Campbell "Charles L. Campbell") and [Robert Rutledge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Rutledge "Robert Rutledge")). It received a further three nominations: [Best Original Screenplay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Screenplay "Academy Award for Best Original Screenplay") (Gale and Zemeckis); [Best Sound](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound "Academy Award for Best Sound") ( [Bill Varney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Varney "Bill Varney"), [B. Tennyson Sebastian II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B._Tennyson_Sebastian_II "B. Tennyson Sebastian II"), [Robert Thirlwell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Thirlwell "Robert Thirlwell"), and [William B. Kaplan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_B._Kaplan "William B. Kaplan")); and [Best Original Song](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song "Academy Award for Best Original Song") ("The Power of Love").[\[156\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Oscars1986-166)

At the [39th British Academy Film Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/39th_British_Academy_Film_Awards "39th British Academy Film Awards"), _Back to the Future_ received five nominations, including [Best Film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Film "BAFTA Award for Best Film"), [Best Original Screenplay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Original_Screenplay "BAFTA Award for Best Original Screenplay") (Gale and Zemeckis), [Best Visual Effects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Special_Visual_Effects "BAFTA Award for Best Special Visual Effects") (Pike and Ralston), [Best Production Design](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Production_Design "BAFTA Award for Best Production Design") (Paull), and [Best Editing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Editing "BAFTA Award for Best Editing") (Schmidt and Keramidas).[\[157\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BAFTA86-167) At the [13th Saturn Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/13th_Saturn_Awards "13th Saturn Awards"), the film won three awards: [Best Science Fiction Film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Science_Fiction_Film "Saturn Award for Best Science Fiction Film"), [Best Actor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Actor "Saturn Award for Best Actor") (Fox), and [Best Special Effects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Special_Effects "Saturn Award for Best Special Effects") (Pike).[\[158\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SaturnAward86-168) It also won the [Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugo_Award_for_Best_Dramatic_Presentation "Hugo Award for Best Dramatic Presentation").[\[159\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HugoAward-169) _Back to the Future_ performed well internationally: it won Best Foreign Producer (Spielberg) and Best Foreign Screenplay at the [David di Donatello](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_di_Donatello "David di Donatello") awards (Italy), [Outstanding Foreign Film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan_Academy_Film_Prize_for_Outstanding_Foreign_Language_Film "Japan Academy Film Prize for Outstanding Foreign Language Film") from the [Japan Academy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan_Academy_Film_Prize "Japan Academy Film Prize"), and the [Goldene Leinwand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goldene_Leinwand "Goldene Leinwand") (Germany) for selling more than three million tickets in its first eighteen months.[\[160\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015116-170)

## Post-release

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Post-release")\]

### Home media

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Home media")\]

_Back to the Future_ was released on [VHS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VHS "VHS") on May 22, 1986, priced at $79.95,[\[161\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTImesVHS-171)[\[162\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015122-172) becoming the first film to sell 450,000 units at that price point, and was also the most-rented cassette of the year.[\[163\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBierbaum199078-173)[\[164\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NewYorkTimes1986Casette-174) A sequel was not planned until after _Back to the Future_'s theatrical release, and a "ToBe Continued..." graphic was appended to the end of the home release to promote awareness of future films.[\[165\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HuffPoTBC-175) When _Back to the Future_ was released on [DVD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DVD "DVD") in 2002, the graphic was removed because Gale and Zemeckis wanted it to be faithful to an in-theater experience.[\[162\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015122-172)[\[165\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HuffPoTBC-175)[\[166\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HomeMediaIGN-176) It debuted on [Blu-ray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blu-ray "Blu-ray") in 2010 for the film's 25thanniversary. The release featured a six-part documentary including interviews with the cast and crew, behind-the-scenes footage, deleted scenes, and associated music videos from all three films. The release also included the public debut of footage of Stoltz portraying Marty McFly.[\[k\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-178) For its 35thanniversary in 2020, a remastered [4K](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/4K_resolution "4K resolution") [Ultra HD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultra-high-definition_television "Ultra-high-definition television") version was released on Blu-ray and [Ultra HD Blu-ray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultra_HD_Blu-ray "Ultra HD Blu-ray"). Along with extras included in previous releases, this edition included audition footage and an exploration of the film's props hosted by Gale. Limited edition steel bookcases and a display replicate of the levitating hoverboard from _Back to the Future PartII_ were also available.[\[168\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-HomeMedia35thann-179) For its 40th anniversary in 2025, new Ultra HD Blu-ray editions of all three films with updated steel bookcase artwork will be released.[\[169\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-180)

The [_Back to the Future_ soundtrack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future:_Music_from_the_Motion_Picture_Soundtrack "Back to the Future: Music from the Motion Picture Soundtrack") was released in July 1985 on [cassette tape](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cassette_tape "Cassette tape"), [LP record](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LP_record "LP record"), and [compact disc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compact_disc "Compact disc") (CD).[\[170\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BTTFcomMusic-181) The soundtrack's lead single, "The Power of Love", peaked at number one on the U.S. [_Billboard_ Hot 100](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100 "Billboard Hot 100"). Sales were initially slow, but it eventually peaked at number twelve on the [_Billboard_ 200](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billboard_200 "Billboard 200"), in part because of the success of "The Power of Love".[\[171\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines201594-182) [Silvestri's score](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future:_Intrada_Special_Collection "Back to the Future: Intrada Special Collection") received a limited release in 2009 onCD, containing the film score and unreleased variations.[\[172\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FilmTracksScore-183) The scores for all three _Back to the Future_ films were first released on LPrecord in 2016, individually and as a collection. Silvestri supervised the remaster of the original master recordings, including previously unreleased tracks, and Gale contributed liner notes.[\[173\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Score2016LP-184)

### 2025 re-release

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: 2025 re-release")\]

In celebration of its 40th anniversary, the film will be re-released theatrically for one week only beginning October 31, 2025. This release marks the first time the film will be presented in premium large formats including [IMAX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMAX "IMAX"), [Dolby Cinema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dolby_Cinema "Dolby Cinema"), [4DX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/4DX "4DX") and [D-Box](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D-Box_Technologies "D-Box Technologies").[\[174\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-185)

### Other media

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Other media")\]

See also: [_Back to the Future_ in other media](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_(franchise)#Other_media "Back to the Future (franchise)")

[![refer to caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Back_to_the_Future_The_Ride_at_Universal_Studios_Japan_1.jpg/250px-Back_to_the_Future_The_Ride_at_Universal_Studios_Japan_1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Back_to_the_Future_The_Ride_at_Universal_Studios_Japan_1.jpg) _[Back to the Future: The Ride](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future:_The_Ride "Back to the Future: The Ride")_ at [Universal Studios Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Studios_Japan "Universal Studios Japan") in 2011

In 1985, film merchandising was a relatively new concept, popularized by the [original _Star Wars_ film trilogy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Wars_original_trilogy "Star Wars original trilogy") (1977–1983).[\[175\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesJun89-186) As _Back to the Future_ was not specifically aimed at children, there was no significant merchandising accompanying its release.[\[176\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SyFyMerch-187) Although a novelization by [George Gipe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Gipe "George Gipe") was released in 1985,[\[177\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-i09Novel-188) one of the earliest items for children, a rideable DeLorean, was not released until 1986.[\[176\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SyFyMerch-187) The film and its sequels have since been represented across a wide variety of merchandise including: [Playmobil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Playmobil "Playmobil"), playing cards, clothing, pottery, posters,[\[178\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EmpireMerch-189) board games,[\[178\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EmpireMerch-189)[\[179\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NewsweekMerch-190) sculpted figures, plush toys,[\[179\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NewsweekMerch-190) [Funko](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Funko "Funko") POP! figures, action figures,[\[176\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SyFyMerch-187) [Hot Wheels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_Wheels "Hot Wheels") and [die-cast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Die-cast_toy "Die-cast toy") vehicles,[\[176\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SyFyMerch-187)[\[180\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015232-191) books, music albums,[\[181\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-PCMagMerch-192) and Christmas ornaments.[\[180\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015232-191)

_Back to the Future_ received several video game adaptations. _[Back to the Future](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_(1985_video_game) "Back to the Future (1985 video game)")_ was released alongside the film for the [Amstrad CPC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amstrad_CPC "Amstrad CPC"), [Commodore 64](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commodore_64 "Commodore 64"), and [ZX Spectrum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ZX_Spectrum "ZX Spectrum").[\[182\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-CGMSpectrum-193)[\[183\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOGGames-194)[\[184\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAmstradAction198713-195) An arcade-adventure game, _[Back to the Future](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_(1989_video_game) "Back to the Future (1989 video game)")_, was released in 1989 for the [Nintendo Entertainment System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nintendo_Entertainment_System "Nintendo Entertainment System"). Gale called it one of the worst games ever made and advised people against purchasing it.[\[183\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOGGames-194)[\[185\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-GeeksandSundry-196) _[Back to the Future: The Pinball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future:_The_Pinball "Back to the Future: The Pinball")_ was released in 1990, although Fox refused permission for the game to use his likeness.[\[185\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-GeeksandSundry-196) An [episodic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Episodic_video_game "Episodic video game") [graphic adventure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graphic_adventure_game "Graphic adventure game") game, _[Back to the Future: The Game](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future:_The_Game "Back to the Future: The Game")_, was released in 2010. Gale contributed to the game's narrative, which takes place after the events of the third film.[\[185\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-GeeksandSundry-196)[\[186\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-PasteMagLegacy-197) An area in _[Lego Dimensions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lego_Dimensions "Lego Dimensions")_ is based on _Back to the Future_ and features voice work by Lloyd.[\[185\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-GeeksandSundry-196)[\[187\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EWGame-198)

_[Back to the Future: The Ride](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future:_The_Ride "Back to the Future: The Ride")_, a [simulator ride](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simulator_ride "Simulator ride"), ran from 1991 to 2007 at [Universal Studios Hollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Studios_Hollywood "Universal Studios Hollywood") and [Universal Studios Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Studios_Florida "Universal Studios Florida"). The ride's development was supervised by Spielberg and featured Doc Brown (Lloyd) chasing down Biff (Wilson) who has stolen the DeLorean. A version of the ride at [Universal Studios Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Studios_Japan "Universal Studios Japan") ran from 2001 to 2016.[\[186\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-PasteMagLegacy-197)[\[188\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NPRPopCulture-199) A _Back to the Future_-themed [Monopoly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monopoly_(game) "Monopoly (game)") board game was released in 2015.[\[178\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EmpireMerch-189)[\[189\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SlashMonopoly-200) A Funko board game was released in 2020. It casts players as one of the main characters from the films to battle different Tannens across history.[\[179\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NewsweekMerch-190)[\[190\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DigitalSpyFunko-201)

There have been several books about the making of the film series. _We Don't Need Roads: The Making of the Back to the Future Trilogy_ is an oral history by those involved in the production.[\[188\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NPRPopCulture-199) _Back to the Future: The Ultimate Visual History_, a book chronicling the development of the entire _Back to the Future_ franchise, was released in 2015.[\[191\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-UproxxVisualHistory-202) The [British Film Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Film_Institute "British Film Institute") released _BFI Film Classics: Back to the Future_ about the film's background.[\[181\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-PCMagMerch-192) The series also includes comic books detailing Doc's and Marty's adventures before and after the events depicted in the films.[\[192\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-THRComicBooks-203) A crossover between the _Back to the Future_ and _[Transformers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transformers "Transformers")_ franchises included a transforming DeLorean toy and associated comic books.[\[193\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-MerchTransformers-204)

## Thematic analysis

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Thematic analysis")\]

### Parental relationships and fate

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Parental relationships and fate")\]

The main theme of _Back to the Future_ concerns taking control and personal responsibility over one's destiny: a situation can be changed even if it seems otherwise impossible to overcome.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10) Thompson said the film represents how one moment can have a significant and lasting impact on a person's life.[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)[\[45\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AVClubThompson-50) Gale believed Doc provided the perfect summary of the series' running theme, when in _[Back to the Future Part III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_Part_III "Back to the Future Part III")_ he said: "Your future is whatever you make it, so make it a good one."[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)

At the start of the film, Marty is rejected at Battle of the Bands and admits he fears his ambitions will remain unrealized. He worries he will end up like his parents and sees direct evidence in 1955 of George, also afraid of rejection, and being unable to approach Lorraine; his fears risk Marty's future.[\[89\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOG88things-94)[\[194\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-UproxxAnalysis-205) Marty sets about manipulating the past to ensure his survival without concern for what impact his presence in 1955 is having on others. On his return to 1985, he is rewarded with wealthier parents and a nicer car, but he has simultaneously damaged Biff's future, reducing him to a valet for the McFlys.[\[46\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AVClubGlover-51)[\[195\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LATimesHoldUp-206) Glover criticized the morality of the film's ending, believing Marty's reward should be happy parents in love with each other, and considered it a result of the film serving corporate interests, promoting the accumulation of wealth and purchasing material objects.[\[46\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AVClubGlover-51) In 2015, Zemeckis said the ending was perfect for its time but would be different if he made it now, although Gale disagreed and said he did not apologize for the scene. American audiences generally had no issue with this ending, but it was criticized by some international audiences.[\[196\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015124-207)

Despite rejection by film studios for not being raunchy enough,[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) _Back to the Future_ alludes to sexual assault, racism, and the [Oedipus complex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oedipus_complex "Oedipus complex") – a psychiatric theory suggesting a child holds an unconscious sexual desire for their opposite-sexed parent, as in the relationship between Marty and his future mother Lorraine in 1955.[\[118\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1985PostMortemCanby-123)[\[195\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LATimesHoldUp-206) The relationships between parents and children are the basis of many elements of the film. Thompson believed the film had remained relevant to new generations because of its core idea that Marty's and the viewer's parents were once children and had the same dreams and ambitions they do.[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)[\[19\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-CNNGaleInterview-21)[\[45\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AVClubThompson-50)

### Reaganism and American anxieties

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Reaganism and American anxieties")\]

[![refer to caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/The_Reagans_with_Michael_J._Fox_and_Nancy_McKeon.jpg/250px-The_Reagans_with_Michael_J._Fox_and_Nancy_McKeon.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Reagans_with_Michael_J._Fox_and_Nancy_McKeon.jpg)(Left to right) [Nancy McKeon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nancy_McKeon "Nancy McKeon"), Michael J. Fox, [Nancy Reagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nancy_Reagan "Nancy Reagan"), and U.S. President [Ronald Reagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan "Ronald Reagan") in October 1985. _Back to the Future_ has been interpreted as an endorsement of Reagan-era policies concerning the American dream, self-reliance, initiative, and technological advancement.

Critics [Justin Chang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justin_Chang "Justin Chang") and Mark Olsen suggest the film can be seen as promoting [Reaganism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reaganism "Reaganism") – the political positions of president Ronald Reagan – which endorses older values of the American dream, initiative, and technological advancement. The Hill Valley of 1985 is depicted as run down and in decay, while in 1955 it is presented as a more simplistic and seemingly safer time, seen through a nostalgic lens.[\[195\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LATimesHoldUp-206) Marty's future is bettered because he goes back to 1955 and teaches George to be more assertive and self-reliant; his initiative leads to a more prosperous future for Marty with materialistic rewards.[\[194\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-UproxxAnalysis-205)[\[195\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LATimesHoldUp-206) The film uses many brand names of the time, ostensibly to make the setting more realistic, e.g. [Mountain Dew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mountain_Dew "Mountain Dew"), [Pepsi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pepsi "Pepsi"), and [Texaco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texaco "Texaco"), but the filmmakers received financial compensation from the brand owners, making their inclusion promotional and commercialistic instead of artistic.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10)[\[194\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-UproxxAnalysis-205)

Film studies lecturer SorchaNí Fhlainn argues that many 1980s films resulted from the American public's desire for escapism from cultural anxieties and fears, including nuclear proliferation, unemployment, crime, growing inequality, and the AIDS crisis. In her view, films like those of the _[Star Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Wars "Star Wars")_ series and _Back to the Future_ offered a childlike reassurance of safety and comfort, emphasizing idealized American values and the positive effects of instilling power in a patriarchal figure like George McFly or Darth Vader.[\[197\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEN%C3%AD_Fhlainn20145-208) English professor Susan Jeffords considered Doc Brown to be an analog for Reagan, a man who embraces technological advancement, who conflicts with Libyan terrorists and provides the means for a failing family to better themselves.[\[198\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEN%C3%AD_Fhlainn20147-209)

The song "Johnny B. Goode" by Chuck Berry is used during the film's final act. Berry initially resisted allowing the song to be used in the film. [NPR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NPR "NPR") argued that while Berry's resistance may have been a matter of money, there are underlying racial issues involved in Marty, a [white male](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_American "White American"), seemingly rewriting history to invent the [rock and roll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rock_and_roll "Rock and roll") music genre, which was heavily influenced by African-American music.[\[188\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NPRPopCulture-199)[\[195\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LATimesHoldUp-206) The 1955 segment also presents a distorted view of America, showing an African-American band playing at the high school dance, which would have been disallowed.[\[152\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LATimesReview-161) Similarly, the African-American character Goldie Wilson is seemingly inspired to work towards becoming mayor by Marty's intervention, inspiring a Reagan-style initiative and self-reliance.[\[194\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-UproxxAnalysis-205)

### Influences

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Influences")\]

As film fans, Gale and Zemeckis's influences are seen throughout _Back to the Future_. There are references to _[The Wizard of Oz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film) "The Wizard of Oz (1939 film)")_ (1939), _[The Shaggy Dog](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Shaggy_Dog_(1959_film) "The Shaggy Dog (1959 film)")_ (1959), _[Dr. Strangelove](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dr._Strangelove "Dr. Strangelove")_ (1964), _Close Encounters of the Third Kind_ (1977), the _Star Wars_ film series, and television shows including _[Mister Peabody](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mister_Peabody "Mister Peabody")_, _[Star Trek: The Original Series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series "Star Trek: The Original Series")_, _[The Outer Limits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Outer_Limits_(1963_TV_series) "The Outer Limits (1963 TV series)")_, and _The Twilight Zone_.[\[19\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-CNNGaleInterview-21)[\[89\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOG88things-94) There are also allusions to 1960's _[The Time Machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Time_Machine_(1960_film) "The Time Machine (1960 film)")_ (based on [H. G. Wells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H._G._Wells "H. G. Wells")'s 1895 [novella of the same name](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Time_Machine "The Time Machine")) and _[A Connecticut Yankee in King Arthur's Court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_Connecticut_Yankee_in_King_Arthur%27s_Court "A Connecticut Yankee in King Arthur's Court")_ by [Mark Twain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Twain "Mark Twain"), in which the central character seemingly moves through time.[\[199\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEN%C3%AD_Fhlainn2015165,_166-210) The DeLorean dashboard chronometer uses the same color scheme as the time device of _The Time Machine_.[\[200\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEN%C3%AD_Fhlainn2015167-211) Critic Ray Loynd opined that Doc can be seen as a [King Arthur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_Arthur "King Arthur")-type, with Marty serving as his knight.[\[4\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RevVariety-5)

## Legacy

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Legacy")\]

### Cultural influence

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Cultural influence")\]

[![refer to caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Tom_Wilson_photo_by_Josh_Alder.jpg/250px-Tom_Wilson_photo_by_Josh_Alder.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tom_Wilson_photo_by_Josh_Alder.jpg) [Thomas F. Wilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_F._Wilson "Thomas F. Wilson") in 2011. He began carrying cards containing answers to the repetitive questions he was asked by fans about the _Back to the Future_ series.

Since its release, _Back to the Future_ has remained an enduring popular culture [touchstone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Touchstone_(metaphor) "Touchstone (metaphor)"),[\[188\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NPRPopCulture-199) and in 2007, the United States [Library of Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Library_of_Congress "Library of Congress") selected the film for preservation in the [National Film Registry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Film_Registry "National Film Registry") for being culturally, historically, or aesthetically significant.[\[201\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-LOC-212) The film elevated Fox from a financially struggling actor to one of the most in-demand and globally recognized stars in Hollywood,[\[202\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimes1986August8-213)[\[34\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesFoxInterview-37) and Gale received fan mail for decades after its release. He said he understood the continuing appreciation for the original film as it was the "purest" and "most complete" in the series.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BOMGaleInterview-10) Fox compared it to _The Wizard ofOz_ (1939), saying it still appeals to children because they do not think of it as an old film.[\[203\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EWFoxLasting-214) In 2012, Thompson called it the greatest role of her career.[\[45\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AVClubThompson-50) Dean Cundey believed it resonated with fans because it offers the fantasy of going back in time to change things and make the present better.[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)[\[204\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EWWilsonCards-215) Lloyd described being approached by fans from around the world, who have said the film inspired them to become a scientist.[\[205\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015241-216)

Many of the principal cast have reunited since the film's release. Often these reunions are for charity, including [The Michael J. Fox Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Michael_J._Fox_Foundation "The Michael J. Fox Foundation") for [Parkinson's disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease "Parkinson's disease") (Fox was diagnosed with the disease at age29), and [Project HOPE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Project_HOPE "Project HOPE").[\[l\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-220) A 2019 reunion for the [TCM Classic Film Festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TCM_Classic_Film_Festival#TCM_Classic_Film_Festival "TCM Classic Film Festival") featured the 4Krestoration premiere of _Back to the Future_.[\[209\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EWTCM-221) During the 2020 [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic "COVID-19 pandemic"), [Josh Gad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josh_Gad "Josh Gad") hosted a _Back to the Future_ retrospective featuring many cast and crew.[\[210\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RollingStoneReunitedApart-222) The cast has also appeared in advertisements only loosely related to _Back to the Future_, trading on their associated popularity.[\[211\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015242-223)

The film has global popular appeal, particularly in the United States, the United Kingdom, France, Argentina, the [Netherlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netherlands "Netherlands"), and Japan.[\[212\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015240%E2%80%93241-224) On October21, 2015 (the day Doc and Marty travel to at the end of _Back to the Future_, as depicted in _Back to the FutureII_) an estimated 27million social media users discussed the films; the most active users were in the United States, Mexico, the United Kingdom, Canada, and Brazil.[\[188\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NPRPopCulture-199)[\[213\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EW2015SocialMedia-225) Ronald Reagan was also a fan, referring to the film during his [1986 State of the Union Address](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986_State_of_the_Union_Address "1986 State of the Union Address") to appeal to America's young voters, saying, "Never has there been a more exciting time to be alive, a time of rousing wonder and heroic achievement. As they said in the film _Back to the Future_, 'Where we're going, we don't need roads.'"[\[188\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NPRPopCulture-199)[\[214\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-CSpanReagan-226)[\[215\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesReaganSpeech-227) Although Gale has said that Reagan, after enjoying the joke about Doc Brown's incredulous response to him becoming president, ordered the theater's projectionist to stop the film, roll it back, and run it again, this is disputed by Reagan's advisor, Mark Weinberg.[\[194\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-UproxxAnalysis-205)[\[216\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg2018a147%E2%80%93150-228)[\[217\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-PoliticoReagan-229) _Back to the Future_ is also seen as responsible for a resurgence of skateboarding in the 1980s.[\[218\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesSkateboard-230)[\[19\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-CNNGaleInterview-21) It made skateboarding a mainstream pastime acceptable for all, not just rebellious teenagers.[\[219\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015236-231)

_Back to the Future_ has been referred to in a variety of media, including television,[\[155\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEN%C3%AD_Fhlainn20142-165)[\[220\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureStranger-232) films,[\[221\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EWMillion-233)[\[222\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-THREndgame-234) and video games.[\[223\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-GTAV-235)[\[224\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EWRocketLeague-236) Doc and Marty, respectively, inspired the eponymous characters of the 2013 animated television show _[Rick and Morty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rick_and_Morty "Rick and Morty")_.[\[225\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AVClubRandM-237) The British pop rock band [McFly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McFly "McFly") are named for Marty McFly.[\[226\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-McFlySite-238) The 2011 novel _[Ready Player One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ready_Player_One "Ready Player One")_ by [Ernest Cline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernest_Cline "Ernest Cline") and the [2018 film adaptation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ready_Player_One_(film) "Ready Player One (film)") (directed by Spielberg) both heavily refer to the film, including the central character using a DeLorean for transport.[\[227\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RPO1-239)[\[228\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RPO2-240) Filmmaker [J. J. Abrams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._J._Abrams "J. J. Abrams") has also cited it as an inspiration.[\[52\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-WiredHardin-57)

The 2015 [crowdfunded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crowdfunding "Crowdfunding") documentary _[Back in Time](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_in_Time_(2015_film) "Back in Time (2015 film)")_ follows various fans of the series and details the impact it has had on their lives, interspersed with interviews from the crew including Fox and Lloyd.[\[229\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SyFyBackinTime-241) The DeLorean is considered one of the most iconic vehicles in film history.[\[230\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EWDeLorean-242) DeLorean's creator [John DeLorean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_DeLorean "John DeLorean") was a fan of the film and sent personal letters to Gale and Zemeckis, thanking them for using his vehicle.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EsquireDidntGetMade-11) The DeLorean was not a popular vehicle before the film's release. However, in the years since it has become a popular collector's item, the [DeLorean Motor Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DeLorean_Motor_Company "DeLorean Motor Company") issued kits enabling fans to make their vehicle look like the DeLorean time machine.[\[38\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VultureLostRoles-41)[\[186\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-PasteMagLegacy-197) Gale led a restoration of one of the original screen-used DeLoreans in 2011, documented in _Out of Time: Saving the DeLorean Time Machine_.[\[186\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-PasteMagLegacy-197)[\[231\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BTTFcomDelorean-243)[\[232\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-VergeDelorean-244)

### Modern reception

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Modern reception")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Back_to_the_Future_Reunion_NYCC_8.jpg/250px-Back_to_the_Future_Reunion_NYCC_8.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Back_to_the_Future_Reunion_NYCC_8.jpg) Christopher Lloyd and Michael J. Fox discussing the film at the 2022 [New York Comic Con](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Comic_Con "New York Comic Con")

_Back to the Future_ is considered a landmark of American cinema, and one of the greatest films ever made.[\[m\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-247) In 2004, _The New York Times_ listed it as one of the 1,000 Best Movies Ever,[\[235\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-NYTimesBest-248) and the following year its screenplay was listed as the 56th greatest screenplay of the preceding 75 years by the [Writers Guild of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America "Writers Guild of America").[\[236\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-WGAGreatest1-249)[\[237\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-WGAGreatest2-250) Throughout the rest of the 2000s, it appeared on [Film4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Film4 "Film4")'s _[50 Films to See Before You Die](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/50_Films_to_See_Before_You_Die "50 Films to See Before You Die")_ (number10),[\[238\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Film4Die-251) _[Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_(magazine) "Empire (magazine)")_'s 500 Greatest Movies of All Time (number23), behind the 1977 space opera _[Star Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Wars_(film) "Star Wars (film)")_,[\[233\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Empire500-245) and the [American Film Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Film_Institute "American Film Institute") listed it as the number10 best science fiction film, based on a poll of fifteen hundred people from the creative community.[\[239\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-AFITop10-252) In 2010, _[Total Film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Total_Film "Total Film")_ named it one of the 100 greatest movies ever made, and the following year it was voted by [BBC Radio 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_Radio_1 "BBC Radio 1") and [BBC Radio 1Xtra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_Radio_1Xtra "BBC Radio 1Xtra") listeners as their fourth favorite film of all time.[\[240\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TotalFilmGreatest-253)[\[241\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BBCRADIO1-254) It is also listed in the film reference book _[1001 Movies You Must See Before You Die](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1001_Movies_You_Must_See_Before_You_Die "1001 Movies You Must See Before You Die")_.[\[242\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneider2013-255) A 2014 poll of 2,120 entertainment-industry members by _The Hollywood Reporter_ ranked it as the 12th best film of all time, again behind _Star Wars_.[\[234\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-THRJun14-246) In 2015, the screenplay was listed as the 67th funniest on the WGA's 101 Funniest Screenplays list,[\[243\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-WGAFunniest1-256)[\[244\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-WGAFunniest2-257) and _Rotten Tomatoes_ also listed the film at number84 on its list of 200 essential movies to watch.[\[245\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RT200-258)

Several publications have named it as one of the best science fiction films ever made,[\[n\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-271) and one of the best films of the 1980s.[\[o\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-287) _[Popular Mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Mechanics "Popular Mechanics")_ and _Rolling Stone_ listed it as the numberone and numberfour best time-travel film ever made respectively.[\[273\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BestTimeTravelPopMec-288)[\[274\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BestTimeTravelRS-289) _Entertainment Weekly_ named it the 40th most essential film to be watched by pre-teens and the 28th best high-school movie.[\[275\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EWHighSchool-290)[\[276\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BestforKidsEW-291) Marty McFly appeared at number39 on _Empire_'s 2006 list of its "100 Greatest Movie Characters"; Doc Brown followed at number76.[\[277\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Empire100Marty-292)[\[278\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Empire100Doc-293)

_Rotten Tomatoes_ assesses a 93% approval rating from the aggregated reviews of 112 critics, with an average rating of 8.8/10. The site's consensus reads: "Inventive, funny, and breathlessly constructed, _Back to the Future_ is a rousing time-travel adventure with an unforgettable spirit."[\[279\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RottenTomatoes-294) Based on this score, Rotten Tomatoes also listed it as the 87th best Action and Adventure film.[\[280\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-BestActAdvRT-295) The film has a score of 87 out of 100 on [Metacritic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metacritic "Metacritic") based on 15 critics, indicating "universal acclaim".[\[281\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Metacritic-296) In the United Kingdom, readers of _Empire_ voted the film as 11th on their 2017 list of "The 100 Greatest Movies".[\[282\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-Empire2-297)

## Sequels and adaptations

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Back_to_the_Future&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Sequels and adaptations")\]

Main articles: [_Back to the Future_ (franchise)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_(franchise) "Back to the Future (franchise)"), [_Back to the Future Part II_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_Part_II "Back to the Future Part II"), and [_Back to the Future Part III_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_Part_III "Back to the Future Part III")

A sequel was not initially planned, and the teaser ending of Doc, Marty, and Jennifer flying off in the DeLorean suggested their adventures would continue off-screen.[\[89\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOG88things-94) Universal Pictures was eager to pursue a sequel based on the significant financial and critical success of _Back to the Future_. However, Zemeckis and Gale were reluctant to participate, believing sequels often retread the best elements of the original film. They were also concerned that a poor follow-up could alienate _Back to the Future_'s passionate fan base, and undermine the pair after their first major joint success. Zemeckis and Gale acquiesced by 1987, once Universal Pictures clarified they would, if necessary, make a sequel without them.[\[283\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaines2015117%E2%80%93118,_128-298) The pair's sequel script was so long it was split into two films, _Back to the Future PartII_ (1989) and _Back to the Future PartIII_ (1990); the films were shot back to back.[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-TheGuardianHowWeMade-15)[\[284\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOGBTTF2-299)

_Part II_ depicts Marty and Doc traveling to 2015, inadvertently enabling the now-elderly Biff Tannen to steal the DeLorean and return to 1955, rewriting history in his favor.[\[284\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOGBTTF2-299) Wells and Glover did not return for the sequels.[\[p\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-301) _PartII_ was a financial success but was criticized for its complex, convoluted narrative.[\[286\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-THRSequels-302) Zemeckis has said it is his least favorite film in the series.[\[284\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOGBTTF2-299) The final film, _PartIII_ follows Marty as he travels to 1885 to rescue a time-stranded Doc.[\[287\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-DOGBTTF3-303) While the film fared less well financially than the two earlier films, it was more critically well-received than _PartII_.[\[286\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-THRSequels-302) A 2018 poll by _The Hollywood Reporter_ of 2,200 people found 71% wanted a _Back to the Future_ sequel, ahead of another _[Toy Story](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toy_Story_(franchise) "Toy Story (franchise)")_ or _[Indiana Jones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indiana_Jones "Indiana Jones")_ film.[\[288\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-SkyTHRMostWanted-304) Gale has said there will never be a fourth film, likening it to "selling your kids into prostitution". He added a _Back to the Future_ film could never happen without Fox, who could not participate because of the effects of his Parkinson's disease.[\[289\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RadioTimes4thFilm-305)[\[290\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-EmpireParkinsons-306)

An animated television series, _[Back to the Future](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_(TV_series) "Back to the Future (TV series)")_, aired on [CBS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CBS "CBS") between 1991 and 1992. It follows Doc's and Marty's adventures through various historical periods, intercut with live-action segments featuring Doc (Lloyd), performing science experiments alongside [Bill Nye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Nye "Bill Nye").[\[186\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-PasteMagLegacy-197) A short film, _Doc Brown Saves the World_ (2015), celebrated the film's 30th anniversary. Lloyd reprised his role as Doc, who must travel to the future to prevent a nuclear holocaust in 2045.[\[291\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-ScreenRantSavestheWorld-307) A [musical theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musical_theatre "Musical theatre") production, _[Back to the Future](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_(musical) "Back to the Future (musical)")_, debuted in February 2020 at the [Manchester Opera House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester_Opera_House "Manchester Opera House"), England, to positive reviews. The musical was written by Gale and Zemeckis, with music written by Silvestri and [Glen Ballard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glen_Ballard "Glen Ballard").[\[292\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-MusicalBBC-308)[\[293\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-MusicalStandard-309)[\[294\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-MusicalGuardian-310) Gale described it as the best way to give fans more _Back to the Future_ without adding to the film series.[\[289\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-RadioTimes4thFilm-305) In 2024, Zemeckis said he was interested in adapting the musical into a movie.[\[295\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-IGNMovieMusical-311) Overall, the [_Back to the Future_ franchise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_(franchise) "Back to the Future (franchise)") is considered one of the most successful film franchises in history.[\[19\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-CNNGaleInterview-21)[\[192\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Back_to_the_Future#cite_note-THRComicBooks-203)
